International Commercial Telegram; Reuters Special Commodity Report, April 5th 49

Gold and Silver: British Gold: The London gold price remained largely unchanged, quoted at 143 shillings and 10.5 pence, 4.5 pence lower than yesterday.

British Silver: The London silver market was very quiet. India sold, speculators bought, and China both bought and sold. The spot price was 28.3125 pence, the same as yesterday's price. The futures price was 28.4375 pence, 0.0625 pence higher than yesterday.

Exchange Rates: British-American: The London foreign exchange market was initially firm today but then became quiet. The opening British-American exchange rate was $4.85, 0.375 higher than yesterday's closing rate. It then gradually fell, and at 1:00 PM, the rate was $4.840625, 0.09375 lower than the opening rate. However, at 2:00 PM, the rate rebounded to $4.85, the same as the opening rate.

British-French: The opening price was 73.59 francs, 30 points higher than yesterday's closing price, and then fell 3 points. At noon, it fell another 12 points to 73.44 francs. The price remained unchanged for the next hour, but at 2:00 PM, a surge occurred, bringing it back to 73.59 francs, restoring the opening price.

Exchange Rates: New York Foreign Exchange Market: The British exchange rate opened higher in New York today, with a price of $4.8525, 0.0625 higher than yesterday's closing rate. The French exchange rate was 6.59, half a point lower.

Cotton and Wheat: American Cotton: The New York cotton market opened slightly higher due to high Liverpool telegraph prices, but it soon fell again. Senator Thomas's statement that he would introduce a bill in the Senate to abolish processing fees and subsidize cotton planting expenses did not have an absolutely positive impact.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market was weak today due to speculative selling and a lack of buying interest. Some in the United States believe that wheat prices have reached their highest level. At 1:00 PM, the July futures price was 5 shillings and 7.25 pence, 1 penny lower than yesterday's closing price.

British Cotton: The Liverpool market was better today, with some buying interest. At 1:00 PM, the July futures price was 6.06, 2 points higher than yesterday's closing price.

American Wheat: The Chicago wheat market had a tendency to rebound. The opening price for July futures was 0.0875 lower than yesterday's closing price at 95. Half an inch of rain was seen in the drought areas, and market conditions are expected to ease.

Rubber: London: The London rubber market was more active today, but trading was quiet, with minimal fluctuations. This afternoon, the July and September futures trading prices were 5.6875 pence, 0.0125 lower than yesterday's closing price.

New York: New York rubber opened this morning, with July futures falling 17 points compared to yesterday, and then continued to fall.

Securities: New York: The New York securities market opened with the same steady atmosphere as yesterday, with prices slightly higher than yesterday's close. However, due to news from Paris that the Dutch bank would no longer allow gold to be transported to France, there was general concern about the future of the gold group. As a result, securities rebounded slightly. The prices are as follows:

Nanjing City Government; Provides Funds to Dismiss Refugees 50

(Nanjing) The Nanjing City Government is providing funds to dismiss refugees now that the soup kitchens have been closed. On the 5th, refugees flocked to the City Government to petition. Nearly 10,000 people gathered at the distribution point at Wuding Gate, and the situation was serious. All military and police agencies were dispatched to maintain order before it subsided. This case was originally handled by the Social Affairs Bureau, which sent a letter to the Police Department to compile a roster of refugees eating at the soup kitchens and issue dismissal fees of yuan each according to the list, totaling about 6,000 people. Another group of refugees did not receive the payment and again petitioned the City Government on the 4th. They were then distributed payments by name inside Bailuzhou. The large number of poor people in the vicinity crowded in to join, making it impossible to control. On the morning of the 5th, a large group surrounded the City Government to request distributions. As the number of people continued to gather, the City Government consulted with the Police Department and agreed to give each person one jiao, which was distributed at Wuding Gate. People rushed to be first, and traffic at both city gates was blocked, causing chaos and disorder. Troops were sent with bullets, but fortunately, no incidents occurred. About 1,000 yuan was distributed. In total, there were about 10,000 people, and they dispersed in the evening. A total of 4,744 yuan was distributed in two days, and about 1,000 yuan was distributed today. There were instances of people receiving payments multiple times. Anyone who received a payment had an indelible silver dye applied to their finger. (Special Dispatch, 5th)

(Nanjing) Nanjing City Citizen Representative Lü Shou-nan and five others telegraphed Chairman Chiang on the 5th, saying, "Your Excellency's visit to Sichuan and prohibition of harsh levies have given the people of Sichuan a new lease on life. Last year, Jiangsu experienced a drought, and the disaster-stricken people have no clothing or food. In the capital alone, tens of thousands of starving people are eating at soup kitchens. With spring plowing imminent, they cannot return home. It is heart-wrenching to see. I sigh deeply. I rely on Your Excellency to order the Nanjing City and Jiangsu Provincial Governments to immediately stop urging the payment of overdue housing donations, grain taxes, and business taxes, and to exempt them from collection. We await your urgent orders." (Special Dispatch, 5th)

Ministry of Transportation; Unifies National Postage Rates 51

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Transportation believes that the postage rates for letters and postcards in border areas are higher than in other provinces, which is highly inappropriate. In order to facilitate communication for people in border areas, it has been decided to unify postage rates so that they are the same as in other provinces. This has been submitted to the Executive Yuan for discussion, ordering the post office to make corrections. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 5th)

Three-Level, Three-Trial System to be Implemented First in Shandong, Anhui, and Hubei 52

(Nanjing) The area for the first implementation of the three-level, three-trial court organization law, which the Ministry of Justice plans to implement from July 1st of this year, has been decided to be the three provinces of Shandong, Anhui, and Hubei. The other provinces are still under careful consideration and have not been completely decided. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 5th)

(Chongqing) Liu Xiang told reporters that the governor's office has been issuing funds to the Sichuan army since March, having already issued 2,183,000 yuan, which is more abundant and complete than when the various armies collected their own funds in the past. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 5th)

Style of Correspondence Between District Courts and County Governments Concurrently Handling Judicial Affairs 59

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Judicial Administration recently issued a notice to various High Courts, explaining the style of correspondence between the Chief Prosecutor of the District Court and the county government concurrently handling judicial affairs as follows: When the prosecutor directs enforcement, it should be done in writing in accordance with the provisions of the first paragraph of Article 478 of the Criminal Procedure Law. When returning case files, the official letter should still be used in accordance with the instructions of the Judicial Yuan No. 25 of the 18th year. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 5th)

Factory Law; Case of Banning Night Work for Female Workers 60

(Nanjing) Regarding the case of banning night work for female workers under Article 13 of the Factory Law, it has been resolved at the 450th meeting of the Central Political Committee to extend the preparatory period for the implementation of that article until August 1st of next year. The National Government has already issued instructions to the Executive Yuan on the 4th to comply. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 5th)

Judicial Yuan Explains Ambiguity Regarding Punishment for Stealing a Land Deed 61

(Nanjing) The Judicial Yuan recently explained the ambiguity regarding the punishment for stealing a land deed as follows: (1) A land deed is not real estate, but rather a documentary proof of real estate. Stealing a land deed should still constitute the crime of theft. (2) A land deed belongs to one kind of ordinary document and is not a security. (Central News Agency Dispatch, 5th)

Northwest Inspection Notes 99

— By Our Special Correspondent Ya

Discussions with Gansu Province Chairman Zhu on Opium Suppression and Cotton Planting

After the reporter returned to Lanzhou, the center of the country, he immediately visited Zhu Shaoliang, the Chairman of the Provincial Government. According to him, "Gansu Province's imports and exports have always been in deficit. Exports have been no more than 20 million yuan in recent years, while imports have been as high as 60 million yuan, a difference of more than 40 million yuan. The nation's foreign trade deficit has increased sharply, leading to the decline of the national economy. Gansu Province's deficit is so huge, which is naturally making it more impoverished. The province's main export goods are hides and furs, followed by medicinal materials and opium. (Opium leaves have insecticidal properties and are important for agriculture. In the past, they were sold well in the three northeastern provinces). The main imports are textiles, followed by iron, paper, and cultural supplies, Western medicine, gasoline, and machine oil, etc. In total, most of the imported goods are related to clothing, food, housing, and transportation. We are now hiring experts to research substitutes. With raw materials such as iron ore and wood, we can make paper and ironware. According to the soil and climate of each county, we are first promoting the planting of cotton, and secondly, the planting of sesame. The climate and soil of most of Gansu are suitable for cotton cultivation, but in reality, only a few counties plant cotton. Apart from Longnan, which is barely self-sufficient, the northeast mostly relies on Shaanxi cotton, and the west mostly relies on Xinjiang. Sesame is mostly scattered throughout the region, especially abundant in Longnan West Road. American rayon is originally made from this material. Gansu hemp fiber is of better quality and color than that produced in Jiangxi, only slightly inferior in length, so it can also be used to help solve the problem of clothing shortage. Other measures include developing the Yumen oil field, refining gasoline, and using residual oil to replace imported machine oil. We have entrusted the airline company to send samples to Germany for chemical testing, and there is a good possibility of success. The area occupied by opium planting is considerable. Once strict prohibition is implemented, in order to avoid the problem of low grain prices harming farmers if everyone switches to grain cultivation, we must select other crops, such as cotton, hemp, and indigo, to replace opium. We are now supervising the relevant agencies to actively research and experiment. Opium planting in twenty provinces has been repeatedly banned and relaxed, and the harm caused is beyond words. Five or six years ago, Gansu opium could still be sold to various ports in Zhili and Shanghai, which could slightly help the rural economy of the province. In recent years, the Tianjin market has been seized by Rehe opium, and the upper and middle reaches of the Yangtze River are filled with Sichuan and Yunnan opium. The special tax of six jiao per tael transported to Shanghai and Hankou makes the cost too high, and it will be impossible to sell. In this way, Gansu goods will inevitably turn from exports to domestic sales. The position of adjusting the economy in the past has been completely swept away, and the great disaster of harming families and weakening the race is deepening with each passing day. Therefore, Gansu is determined to suppress opium, which is a major policy for the future. We are currently working with the central government to plan implementation methods. Once Gansu's military expenses can be fully paid by the central government, or if other appropriate methods are used to slightly alleviate Gansu's financial difficulties, then the prohibition of planting and smoking can be implemented immediately, and we can guarantee to achieve the great effect of complete prohibition within three years. Recently, we have been advocating and promoting the planting of cotton and hemp, and the authorities in each county have been informing opium farmers to first reduce the amount of smoking, and even extend to the addiction to foreign cigarettes, as well as advocating the use of local opium medicines. All of these can be taken as a prelude to determined opium suppression. As for development issues, we have always advocated that whether it is transportation, water conservancy, agriculture, forestry, mining, or education and culture, there must be detailed research and planning to ensure balanced development without any neglect. Gansu Province has great potential in mining, agriculture, and forestry, but due to local poverty, all the benefits are abandoned on the ground. If the financial and industrial circles are willing to invest in development, the local authorities and people will gladly welcome it." It is said that the cotton in Gansu Province in the past, the flowers and catkins of each plant are not inferior to Shaanxi cotton. Only the seeds are not good, the cultivation is not proper, and most farmers have no cotton-growing experience, and know little about the timing of cotton season, resulting in very few counties that plant cotton, and the results are very poor. According to a survey by the Department of Construction, there are only a few hundred mu to one or two thousand mu of cotton fields in 12 counties including Huixian, Zhenning, Tianshui, Chengxian, Gaotai, Dunhuang, Wudu, Wenxian, Jingyuan, Gaolan, Liangdang, and Wushan. The annual production of cotton lint is 70,388 dan, which is 261,496 dan short compared with the amount of cotton needed by the population of the province. At a price of 5 jiao per jin, the people of the province must spend more than 13 million yuan each year to purchase cotton from other places. If we can do our best to promote the cotton industry in the future, even if we do not have the extravagant hope of exporting, being able to be self-sufficient will already be a bright path for rural areas. According to artist Fan Youxi, "During the fourth and fifth years of the Republic of China, the opium ban in Gansu Province was very strict, and very few opium seedlings were planted. The price of opium was high, selling for eight or nine taels of silver per tael. Opium smokers who could not break their addiction went bankrupt. Many also quit automatically. Compared with the number of opium smokers before the ban, the decrease has reached more than 70%. In the ninth year of the Republic of China, there was an earthquake disaster, and in the tenth year, financial difficulties led to the unfortunate lifting of the ban and the second planting of opium. Because of the high value of opium, farmers flocked to it. During the ban, opium land was changed to cotton fields. At this point, cotton was abandoned and opium was planted again, resulting in a gradual drop in the price of opium and a daily increase in opium smokers. The number of opium smokers today has increased more than 20 times over the number who quit during the ninth year of the Republic. Many new members are young people, and it is customary to set up opium tools as an elegant gift for guests, which is the worst social habit. If this is not quickly corrected, I don't know where it will lead. If opium can be replaced with cotton, it is indeed a good intention and a good method. Taking my hometown of Jingyuan (Fan's county of origin) as an example, it was not originally a cotton-producing area, but during the opium ban, farmers competed to plant cotton. Wang Gongchen in Dongwan Town experimented with the new varieties of defuzzed cotton issued by the construction institute, and each plant was three or four feet tall and flowered about sixty or seventy times, with remarkable results. Other counties in the upper reaches of the Yellow River have similar climates and soils. If it is widely promoted, the effect should also be similar." Fan is good at calligraphy and painting, and in his old age, he pays attention to social education and always uses his spare time to create modern historical dramas for the Gansu and Shaanxi drama troupes. The reporter has visited the Qin Family Garden several times and has read the scripts he has written, which can inspire national consciousness. Now that I have heard these remarks, I am even more clear about the good measures for Gansu Province to suppress opium and promote the cotton industry. I eagerly hope that the authorities' determination will be put into practice as soon as possible, and I hope that financial experts and industrial experts in the southeast will quickly design investment to develop the rich resources of the northwest, so that the power of national capital and industry will establish a prior and deep foundation as early as possible. The impact will not only benefit the northwest region alone.

Jidong Security Forces - Scheduled to Move East for Rotation - Mobilization to Begin on the 10th of This Month - Rotation to be Completed Within This Month 107

Tianjin Correspondence. The issue of the newly reorganized Hebei Security Forces moving east for rotation has been discussed by Gu Tonggu Rugeng and Tao Shangming with Yi Wo and Sakai in Beiping last week. It has been decided to begin implementation on April 10th and complete the rotation within half a month. The old security forces of Fan Jinghe, Yang Yucheng, and Zhou Yuying will be withdrawn from the war zone. Yin and Tao have come to Tianjin from Beiping one after another, and have summoned Zhang Qingyu, the first commander of the new security forces, Zhang Yantian, the second commander, Liu Zuozhou, the first commander of the war zone security, and Zhao Lei, the second commander, to Tianjin to discuss all the procedures for the rotation. Zhang, Liu, Zhao, and others have already arrived. On the afternoon of the 2nd, Yin Tong hosted a banquet in the large living room of the Huayuan on Beining Road to entertain the four security commanders, and invited Liu Zonggan, the chief of staff of the 51st Army, Zhang Houwan, the director of the Civil Affairs Department, Wei Jian, the secretary-general of the Provincial Government, Yin Rugeng, and Tao Shangming to accompany them to discuss the issue of the pre-rotation inspection of the new security forces. On the evening of the 2nd, Yin Tong, Tao Shangming, Yin Rugeng, and Takashi Sakai, the chief of staff of the Japanese army in Tianjin, Ryozo Omaki, the senior staff officer, and Tanaka, the Japanese consul, contacted the inspection procedures, and stated that if it could not be moved on April 10th, it would be opened on the 12th. The Japanese side had no objection to this. At noon on the 3rd, Liu Zonggan, Wei Jian, and Zhang Houwan hosted a banquet for Zhang, Liu Zuozhou, Zhao Lei, the four commanders, and Bantong, Ban Rugeng, Tao Shangming, Zhang Peiwen, the chief of staff of the 51st Army, Cha Yao of the Provincial Committee, Lu Muting, the director of the Department of Finance, Hu Yuanhui, the director of the Department of Construction, Jiang Chunyan, the adjutant of the 51st Army, Zhu Xingyuan, the director of the Foreign Affairs Department, Ren Can, the consultant of the Yuyu Commissioner's Office, and Wang Can, the consultant of the Ji Mi Commissioner's Office, and others. The issue of the new security forces moving east was also discussed at the banquet. At 5:00 PM, Zhang Qingyu and Zhang Yantian returned to their defense areas in Cangzhou and Caicun to prepare everything. Yin Rugeng, Tao Shangming, Zhang Peiwen, the chief of staff of the 51st Army, Jiang Chunyan, the adjutant, Omaki, the staff officer of the Japanese army in Tianjin, and Tanaka, the Japanese consul, have decided to take a car to Caicun and Yangcun early on the 4th to inspect the first team, and then transfer to Cangxian on the 5th to inspect the second team. It is expected that it will be completed on the 6th of this month. At that time, when each team moves east, the Japanese side will send Omaki, Tanaka, Iwa, and Tabashi to monitor in Tangshan and Tongxian. Zhang Qingyu's team will enter the Ji Mi area to take over the first battalion of Zhou Yuying's team in Yutian, and the defense areas of Fan Jinghe's team in Jixian, Zunhua, Huairou, and Miyun. Zhang Yantian's team will enter the Yuyu area to take over the 2nd, 3rd, and 4th battalions of Zhou Yuying in Fangning, and the defense areas of Yang Yucheng's teams in Changli, Qian'an, Leting, Shimen, Beidaihe, and Qinhuangdao. The two teams have recently been reorganized, and each has five battalions, with a total of 500 officers and soldiers per team, a total of 2,500 people, carrying 50 machine guns, 25 per team, and 5 per battalion. As for the defense areas of Liu Zuozhou and Zhao Lei, they remain the same. Only Feng Shoupeng's team will be reorganized into a special independent battalion, consisting of one infantry, cavalry, and artillery company, a total of 360 people. As for the future defense area, it will still be Kaiping. (3rd)

Yellow River Commission Renovates Jin Dike in Sections, Construction Begins, Commission Appoints Wang Zongkui and Zhao Shenshu as Section Chiefs, and Funds for Embankments in Three Provinces Have Been Proposed 108

Kaifeng Correspondence. The Yellow River Conservancy Commission was ordered to renovate the Jin Dike project, and drafted an emergency project plan to renovate the embankments in Henan, Hebei, and Shandong provinces, and determine the method of sharing the funds. Representatives of the three provincial governments and the heads of the river affairs bureaus were convened for a meeting on March 28. It was originally agreed that the Jin Dike section would require 460,000 yuan, all of which would be allocated by the central government and handled by the Yellow River Conservancy Commission. The emergency projects for the embankments in the three provinces totaled nine items, requiring 1.08 million yuan. It was decided that the central government would subsidize 540,000 yuan, and the remainder would be shared by the three provinces. It was recently heard that the Commission received 300,000 yuan in construction funds from the National Economic Commission yesterday (the 1st). The Commission believed that the various projects were very urgent, so it retained 100,000 yuan for the Jin Dike project and allocated the remaining 200,000 yuan to the other embankment projects, which was remitted to Shandong Province by the Central Bank on April 1st, 50,000 yuan to Hebei Province, and 50,000 yuan to Henan Province, and the provincial governments were telegraphed to quickly raise the funds for their responsibility, designate the responsible handling agency, and submit the project plan to the Commission for approval and transfer, and to start construction, and to telegraph the date of commencement and the handling situation. As for the Jin Dike renovation project, the Commission is actively preparing, and section engineering offices have been set up in Puyang, Hebei, and Fanxian, Shandong. The first section is from Huaxian to Gaodikou, the second section is from Gaodikou to Taochengbu. For the first section of the project, the entire staff of the Commission's Second Survey Team was transferred from Jiyang, Shandong, to Fanxian to start work immediately, and the team leader Wang Zongkui was appointed as the section chief. For the second section, the Commission appointed engineer Zhao Shenshu as the section chief. It was also heard that the Chairman of the Commission, Li Yishe, traveled with engineer Liu Bingxi from Bian by train on the way to Zhengzhou Daokou yesterday (2nd) to inspect and plan everything along the Jin Dike in Hanyang and other places. (4th)

Measurement Dispute Resolved 112

Rice merchants from six counties, including Xixian, Su, Kun, Yu, Wu, and Wuxi, have suffered significant losses due to the new dou used in Shanghai being larger than the old by three he per shi. They have repeatedly met to discuss relief measures without reaching a solution. Therefore, the Central Jiangsu County Government notified the examiners of the six counties to bring their measuring instruments to Shanghai for comparison and to attend the Measurement Verification Institute meeting. Representatives from this county Qin Heming, Wu County Wang Ruling, Kunshan Shi Xiguang, Changshu Xu Zhongsheng, Wujin Zhang Tingsheng, and Wujiang Ni Jingying all arrived in Shanghai on time to attend the meeting, which was chaired by Director Zhou Zanming. It was decided that the tolerance for the municipal five-dou measuring instruments used by the rice industry in Shanghai and related counties should not be greater or smaller than half a he during verification, and the tolerance for each measurement should not be greater or smaller than one he during inspection. In early May, the Shanghai Verification Institute will re-verify the new dou used and notify the above counties separately, and report to the Ministry for record. After the meeting, the representatives returned to their respective posts.

Business Tax Dispute Resolved Satisfactorily 117

The Jiangdu Business Tax Bureau found that the reported business amounts of various shops in the urban area were mostly untrue. Therefore, when the tax was collected in the spring of the 24th year, the accounts were first investigated, which aroused resentment from various industries. An emergency meeting was held at the Chamber of Commerce on the afternoon of the 3rd. As a result, Zhu Lizhai and eight others were publicly elected to appeal to the Provincial Committee member Ba Shudong, who was dispatched by the province, on the morning of the 4th, and stated the difficulties of Jiangdu's commerce, requesting understanding. Subsequently, the Provincial Committee put forward three points: (1) The remaining amounts of business income of various industries are exempt from taxation; (2) Shops should clearly separate the wholesale facade accounts to avoid confusion when collecting taxes; (3) The business ratio between the 23rd and 24th years will be considered after the accounts are investigated. Finally, all representatives expressed their acceptance of the account issues, considering it satisfactory.

Zhenjiang: Investigation Begins for Collection of House Tax 120

Regarding the issue of collecting house tax in Jiangsu Province, after it was decided to implement it on July 1st, the province is now ordering various counties to provide detailed reports on existing house tax collections to determine tax methods. According to the initial investigation by the department, about 60% to 70% of the counties in the province are currently collecting house tax, with a total annual amount of about 960,000 yuan. Some rates are as high as several percent, while others are more than 10%, varying widely. It is reported that after the investigation by the financial department is completed, it will re-determine the required amount based on the public security expenses of each county.

The business tax on foil in Jiangsu and Zhejiang has always been contracted by merchants, with a contracted amount of more than 2.2 million per year. Haimen: Chen Pinqi Commits Suicide by Jumping into the River 125

The Xin Renhe transport ship, which travels between Shanghai and Haimen, arrived in Haimen from Shanghai at 6 PM the day before yesterday (2nd). When it reached the outer Wusongkou, a steerage passenger dressed as a worker suddenly jumped into the river and committed suicide. At that time, the southeast wind was strong and the waves were turbulent, making it impossible to rescue him. He was lost in a moment. Later, the crew found an old cap and a suicide note left behind beside the ship's railing. The handwriting was hasty and sparse, with a few words: "The suicide is Chen, please gentlemen, send to the Fajie Xijiang Hospital and hand it over to my brother Lin Qi to receive, brother Pinqi." It was handed over to the accounting room for safekeeping. Later, someone who knew Chen said that Chen lived in Donglaogaoqiao, Shijiazhen, in this county, and worked as a waiter at the Shanghai Siming Bank. Yesterday morning (3rd), the transport ship arrived at Songji Port and ordered someone to notify the family and send the suicide note to Chen Linqi in Shanghai.

Kong Xiangxi Arrives in Shanghai to Discuss the National Economic Construction Movement: Three Banks Can Rescue Various Industries After Capital Increase, Exemption of Transit Tax to Be Implemented on June 1st 127

According to the Central News Agency, Kong Xiangxi, Deputy President of the Executive Yuan and Minister of Finance, took the night train from Nanjing at 11 PM the night before last and arrived at Zhenru at 7:15 AM yesterday morning. He went straight back to his private residence on West Aihams Road to rest and received Song Ziwen, a standing committee member of the National Economic Commission, and Zheng Lai, director of the Customs Administration, for consultations. At noon, he went to the Central Bank to meet Fu Rulin and reporters from various newspapers to deliver the following speech.

National Economic Construction Movement According to Kong, Chairman Jiang has been traveling around the country in recent years, devoting himself to military suppression of bandits. Seeing the suffering of the people in various places and the bankruptcy of the rural areas, he realized the need for national economic construction. Therefore, following the New Life Movement, he advocated national economic construction to enable farmers to work hard in production, reduce consumption, and enable the rural areas to recover. This is the Principle of Livelihood in the Three Principles of the People advocated by Sun Yat-sen. To complete this movement, the government should work hard, and the people should also work hard to achieve success.

Relief for Domestic Industry, Commerce, and Agriculture Regarding the relief for domestic industry, commerce, and rural areas, it is in progress after the Ministry of Finance issued public bonds to replenish the capital of the three banks. Increasing the capital of the three banks is like adding an electric motor to a factory. With a motor, it can generate power and operate. After the three major banks have increased their capital, domestic industry, commerce, and rural areas can be rescued. The government is also seeking to urge the three banks to carry out relief work in a rational and scientific manner.

Zhang Gongquan Decides to Take Office Kong finally said that foreign media reports that he will convene a currency conference of various countries are incorrect. As for Zhang Gongquan's resignation as Vice President of the Central Bank, this is also not true. However, Zhang told him that he would take a short rest after completing the handover of matters at the Bank of China before taking office. Therefore, he has not yet taken office. As for the Ministry of Finance's exemption of transit tax and reduction of export tax, it is now planned to be implemented on June 1st.

The City's Spring Plowing Movement to Begin on the 20th, Decided at the Yesterday's Preparatory Meeting 129

According to the Shenshi News Agency, the Social Affairs Bureau, the Municipal Farmers' Association, the Municipal Party Department, and the Agricultural Experiment Field are jointly holding a large-scale spring plowing movement in the city. Those present included Wu Huanru of the Social Affairs Bureau (representing Yu Zhenhui), Zhang Huijun of the Municipal Farmers' Association, Ji Hao of the Municipal Party Department, and Bao Bodu of the Agricultural Experiment Field. Wu Huanru chaired the meeting, and Zhang Huijun recorded the minutes. The following resolutions and revised spring plowing movement plan were passed.

Discussion Items The chairman reported on the progress of the Social Affairs Bureau in organizing the spring plowing movement according to the order of the ministry, and then discussed: (1) the spring plowing proposed by the Social Affairs Bureau, (2) determining the budget, which was decided to be about 700 yuan, with a detailed budget to be prepared by the Social Affairs Bureau, (3) how to allocate the funds, which was decided to be 60% by the Social Affairs Bureau, 30% by the Municipal Party Department, and 10% by the Municipal Farmers' Association, (4) determining the date of the spring plowing movement, which was decided to start on the 20th of this month with tours, with the order to be followed according to item 6 of the plan, with lectures scheduled for one day in each district, (5) showing agricultural films, which was decided to be borrowed from the Central People's Movement Committee and the Municipal Government Film Association, and (6) that the above resolutions should be handled separately by the Social Affairs Bureau.

Spring Plowing Plan (1) This bureau aims to instill new agricultural knowledge to farmers and improve their production skills. In accordance with the spring plowing movement measures stipulated by the Central People's Movement Committee, the Municipal Party Department, the Municipal Farmers' Association, and other related groups and agencies will hold a spring plowing movement during the spring plowing period. (2) All issues related to agriculture and farmers' lives, such as seed selection, pest control, fertilization, cultivation, farming, animal husbandry, afforestation, disease prevention, improvement of agricultural tools, promotion of various side businesses, road construction, irrigation canals, agricultural transportation, sales, warehousing, and cooperation, are the subjects of the movement. (3) The mode of movement is propaganda and practice, which complement each other. To achieve universal coverage and efficiency, touring lectures will be held. (4) Simple publications and related drawings will be compiled and distributed during the lectures, and specimens related to agriculture will be displayed to make it easier for farmers to understand. (5) Agricultural films will be shown or farmers' gatherings will be held to attract farmers to participate and promote farmers' proper entertainment. (6) The spring plowing movement will be held in the following seventeen districts in order: Wusong, Jiangwan, Yinxiang, Guxing, North Shanghai, Pengpu, Zhenru, Pusong, Caojing, Fahua, Nini, Yangsi, Qiao, Yangjing, Lihang, Gaohang, and Gaoqiao. How to use rural gatherings will be determined separately on a temporary basis. (7) The specimens and propaganda materials required for the touring lectures will be collected and compiled by this bureau. (8) The lecturers for the touring lectures will be assigned by the Municipal Party Department, district party departments, the Municipal Agricultural Experiment Field, the Municipal Farmers' Association, district farmers' associations, and district municipal committee members, or experts will be hired. (9) During the spring plowing movement touring lectures in each district, the municipal committee members and farmers' associations in each district must cooperate. (10) The funds required for the spring plowing movement will be jointly borne by this bureau, the Municipal Party Department, and the Municipal Farmers' Association.

Financial Silk Industry and Military Retrenchment Public Bonds, Principal Repayment Lottery Held Yesterday Morning, Totaling Eight Winning Tickets for 960,000 Yuan, Financial Silk Industry Starts on the 15th and Military Retrenchment Paid at the End of the Month 130

The thirteenth repayment of the principal of the 20th year Financial Short-term Public Bond, the sixth repayment of the principal of the 20th year Jiangsu and Zhejiang Silk Industry Public Bond, and the nineteenth repayment of the principal of the 18th year Military Retrenchment Public Bond were held at the Bankers Association at 10 AM yesterday morning. The financial silk industry will start on the 15th, and the military retrenchment will start at the end of this month. The details are recorded below.

Supervisory Personnel The supervisory personnel present included Jiang Lufu, Director of the Public Bond Division of the Ministry of Finance, Guo Shenrun of the Accounting Department, Jing Guang of the Ministry of Industry, Lin Leming of the General Taxation Department, Wu Bicai of the Municipal Government, Ke Ganchen of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Luo Huizong of the Hankou Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Chen Ganyi of the Silk Industry Fund Management Committee, Ju Zhijing of the First Special District Court, Xu Xinliu of the Bankers Association, Qian Yuansheng of the Money Dealers Association, Jin Wenyuan of the Central Bank, Zhu Qizhen of the Bank of China, Mao Shijian of the Bank of Communications, Pan Yonghe of the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Jin Wenwei of the Yongheng Bank, and Shen Gongjun of the Dalaizhuang, totaling more than 30 people.

Chairman's Report Chairman Jiang Lufu reported that today is the date for the 13th repayment of the principal of the 20th year Financial Short-term Public Bond, the 6th repayment of the principal of the 20th year Jiangsu and Zhejiang Silk Industry Public Bond, and the 19th repayment of the principal of the 18th year Military Retrenchment Public Bond. He was honored to have everyone present to observe. The total amount of the 20th year Financial Short-term Public Bond issued was 80 million yuan. Except for the first to twelfth repayments, which have already been repaid, this is the thirteenth repayment, with two tickets to be drawn, each for 80,000 yuan, totaling 160,000 yuan, which is 2/1000 of the total issuance amount of the bond. Therefore, the drawing method will use the same last three digits as the winning bond. The total amount of the 20th year Jiangsu and Zhejiang Silk Industry Public Bond issued was 6 million yuan. Except for the first to fifth repayments, which have already been repaid, this is the sixth repayment, with five tickets to be drawn, totaling 300,000 yuan, which is 5% of the total issuance amount of the bond. Therefore, the drawing method will use the same last two digits as the winning bond. Also, the total amount of the 18th year Military Retrenchment Public Bond issued was 50 million yuan. Except for the first to eighteenth repayments, which have already been repaid, this is the nineteenth repayment, with one ticket to be drawn, totaling 500,000 yuan, which is 1% of the total issuance amount of the bond. Therefore, the drawing method will also use the same last two digits as the winning bond. The 20th year Financial Short-term Public Bond and the 20th year Jiangsu and Zhejiang Silk Industry Public Bond will be paid starting from the 15th of this month. Except that the Silk Industry Public Bond will be paid by the Central, China, Communications, and National Goods banks, the rest will still be paid by the Central, China, and Communications banks, together with the matured interest. Regardless of the location, national currency will be paid. Please supervise and check the supporting documents and lottery books to carry out the lottery.

Winning Numbers Then, the supervisory staff inspected the supporting documents and lottery books, and the lottery staff carried out the lottery. A total of two tickets were drawn for the 20th year Financial Short-term Public Bond: "No. 782" and "No. 965", repaying 160,000 yuan. A total of five tickets were drawn for the 20th year Jiangsu and Zhejiang Silk Industry Public Bond: "No. 10", "No. 29", "No. 37", "No. 58", and "No. 73", repaying 300,000 yuan. One ticket was drawn for the 18th year Military Retrenchment Public Bond: "No. 60", repaying 500,000 yuan. The total repayment was 960,000 yuan. The financial silk industry will start paying from the 15th, while the military retrenchment will start paying at the end of this month.

The China Merchants' Steam Navigation Company Decides to Use Boxer Indemnity Funds to Build a New River Steamer, Passing it Through the Board of Directors and Submitting it to the Ministry of Transportation 131

The state-run China Merchants' Steam Navigation Company has finalized a plan, approved by the board of directors, to utilize the remaining funds from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity to construct one Yangtze River steamer and two ships for the upper reaches of the Yangtze. Unexpectedly, due to the "Overall Alliance" agreement among Yangtze River shipping companies, changes arose concerning the ships. Therefore, the matter was reconsidered, and a decision has now been reached. The proposed ship design and related calculations are detailed below:

Revised Ship Design: The Yangtze River Seven Shipping Companies have agreed to a business revenue sharing system, eliminating mutual competition to pursue open cooperation. The draft proposal was prepared long ago, emphasizing larger and more economical vessels. Therefore, the ship dimensions determined in the second iteration of the China Merchants' Boxer Indemnity-funded river steamer project are unsuitable. Previously, Liu Hongsheng of the Shipbuilding Department, along with the Chief Ship Surveyor, and Wu Daming, were tasked with redesigning the dimensions for the new river steamer, with a deadline for submission to the General Manager's Office. This would allow for its presentation to the Board of Directors for bidding on construction. In recent days, Shen Jiyun, Wu Daming, and the New Ship Committee have finalized the drawings for the river steamer and submitted them to the Board of Directors for approval, forwarding it to the Ministry of Transportation.

Tonnage and Dimensions: The third new plan involves constructing only one Yangtze River steamer, abandoning the plan for upper Yangtze ships. The tonnage of the new Yangtze River steamer will be increased. The finalized specifications are as follows: hull length (net) of 340 feet, vertical line length of 330 feet, width of 47 feet, depth of 15 feet and 3 inches, and a carrying capacity of 2,800 tons. The draft is classified into three categories: 14 feet carrying 2,800 tons of cargo; 13 feet carrying 2,450 tons; 11 feet 6 inches carrying 2,000 tons; and the shallowest draft of 10 feet 6 inches carrying 1,650 tons. This is the latest type of Yangtze River steamer, capable of operating even during the dry season without being forced to suspend service. The speed is 12 nautical miles per hour.

Ordering Materials: Due to the conditions attached to the Boxer Indemnity funds, the engine components and other materials for the river steamer will be purchased through bidding in the United Kingdom, with a budget of £33,000, equivalent to $429,000 in national currency. The hull, fittings, and cabin arrangements will be constructed at a Shanghai shipyard, with an estimated cost of $450,000. The anticipated shortfall of over $200,000 will be covered by the Bureau through other means. The Bureau has informed the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Board of Directors of this intention, and once approval is received from the Ministry, the engine materials will be purchased in England.

Operating Budget: The Bureau has carefully estimated the operating budget for the new Yangtze River steamer. Assuming 33 voyages per year, each carrying cargo, the revenue from freight charges is estimated at $13,800 per voyage, and passenger fares are estimated at $3,500 per voyage. The total annual freight revenue is $455,400, and passenger fare revenue is $115,500, for a total of $570,900. The estimated expenses are: loading and unloading labor $39,600, dock fees $9,900, coal $79,860, materials $9,600, wages $52,000, interest $67,200, repairs $21,000, insurance $42,000, depreciation $42,000, and miscellaneous expenses $15,000, for a total of $378,160. After deducting expenses, the annual net profit is estimated at $192,740.

Allegations of Illegal Transfer of Chinese Eastern Railway Assets in Shanghai 133

The Shishi News Agency reports that following the establishment of the illegal sale of the Chinese Eastern Railway, the issue of the disposal of the railway's wharf in Shanghai has drawn considerable attention. According to the Shishi News Agency's reporter, the representative of the South Manchuria Railway (Mantetsu), Sumida, along with the director of the Mantetsu Shanghai office, Ishii, have been in negotiations with the Chinese Eastern Railway Shanghai office regarding the transfer. The formal signing took place at 11:00 AM on the fourth at the Mantetsu office, with representatives Talsiff of the Chinese Eastern Railway Shanghai office, Sumida of Mantetsu, and Ishii present. In the afternoon, the three visited the Yangjiadu wharf to inspect and complete the handover procedures. It is reported that the Chinese Eastern Railway office at No. 33 Sichuan Road will be retained by Soviet Russia and renamed the Siberian Railway Shanghai Office.

The North China Daily News reports that yesterday (the 4th), the Japanese Rengo News Agency issued a statement saying that the Chinese Eastern Railway's assets in Shanghai were officially transferred to the management of the Shanghai branch of the South Manchuria Railway Company on Wednesday (the 3rd of this month) afternoon. It also claimed that the necessary documents were signed by the Russian and Japanese authorities. A reporter from the North China Daily News made inquiries, and Tahesis, the manager of the Chinese Eastern Railway's Commercial and Travel Bureau, replied that he had no comment. Ishii, the manager of the Shanghai branch of the South Manchuria Railway Company, stated that the branch had not received any of the Chinese Eastern Railway's assets in Shanghai, nor had it received any documents or books. He said that the transfer had not yet been scheduled and that whether the South Manchuria Railway's Shanghai branch would take over the Chinese Eastern Railway's assets in Shanghai would depend on whether the assets were profitable. He added that he was just beginning to investigate the matter. Mr. Xu Ershi, the lawyer representing the liquidator of the Banque Franco-Chinoise in the lawsuit against the Chinese Eastern Railway Bureau, stated that he could not comment. The matter is confusing and truly perplexing.

Ample Rice Supply in Shanghai, Sufficient Until Autumn Harvest 134

Shanghai rice merchants, previously concerned about the impact of imported rice on the sales of domestic rice, had requested the Ministry of Finance to increase the import tax on broken rice to maintain the market. Subsequently, the Ministry of Finance, in view of the rice shortage and to ensure market equilibrium, sometimes found it necessary to order imported rice. Therefore, it instructed the municipal government to order the Social Affairs Bureau to cease registration (of rice merchants). On the other hand, it planned to set tax rates in mid-June according to the grade requirements of rice. Yesterday, according to a reporter from the Central News Agency, the import of foreign rice, other than goods registered before, has now been completely stopped. There is a large inventory in Shanghai, and the quality of domestic rice is excellent. It is therefore anticipated that the supply can be maintained until the autumn harvest. The market prices in recent days have also been quite stable.

The Central News Agency reports that the Shanghai preview exhibition for the London Exhibition of Chinese Art, which has been in preparation for many days, will open the day after tomorrow (the 8th). Minister of Education Wang Shijie, who is in charge of the exhibition, arrived in Shanghai yesterday to provide on-site guidance for everything. A Central News Agency reporter interviewed the person in charge of the exhibition yesterday, who stated:

Exhibits Added: All antiquities, except those sent by Academia Sinica for the exhibition, have already been properly displayed. The antiquities from the Academia Sinica only arrived at the exhibition hall the day before yesterday. They are all rare items of archaeological interest, totaling one hundred pieces, such as ancient weapons such as spears, which are rarely seen by modern people. They have now been displayed one by one for public viewing. The exhibition hall has also added "Archaeological Selections" to the list of exhibits announced in the preliminary advertisements, in addition to the original paintings, calligraphy, embroidery, bronzes, porcelain, ancient books, jade articles, folding fans, cloisonné, and carved lacquer.

Compilation of Catalogues Available for Sale: A total of approximately one thousand antiquities are on display. To facilitate understanding of the antiquities for the general public, the exhibition hall has specially compiled Chinese and English catalogues, providing detailed explanations. The Chinese catalogue is being printed by the Commercial Press, using Song typeface and Chinese paper, totaling approximately two hundred pages. It is antique and beautiful. It will be sold at cost during the opening, at approximately four or five jiao (cents).

Invitations for Viewing Issued: Wang Shijie, the chairman of the Preparatory Committee and Minister of Education, arrived in Shanghai yesterday. He plans to invite President Wang (Zhaoming) and other government officials in the morning of the 7th, and international dignitaries and newspaper reporters in the afternoon to visit the exhibition. Invitations have already been issued.

Tickets for Admission Entrusted for Sale: To maintain order at the entrance, the exhibition hall has decided not to set up ticket booths at the entrance, and has entrusted the Bank of China on Hankou Road, the Shanghai Bank on Ningbo Road, the China National Goods Company on Nanjing Road, and the China Travel Service on Sichuan Road to sell tickets.

Wang Shijie Issues Statement Yesterday: Minister of Education Wang Shijie arrived in Shanghai from Nanjing the night before last, arriving at 7:00 AM yesterday morning. A reporter from the Central News Agency interviewed him at his residence. According to him, in addition to attending the opening ceremony of the Shanghai preview exhibition of the London Exhibition of Chinese Art, he also plans to attend the preparatory committee of the National Games to be held in Shanghai this year. Regarding the Shanghai preview exhibition of the London Exhibition of Chinese Art, he has not yet visited the exhibition and lacks research in art, so he has no comment. However, all the experts have put in a lot of effort in selecting the antiquities. The five British committee members specially dispatched to China to select antiquities also have special opinions, which were adopted here. It is inevitable that the exhibited antiquities will represent the art of our country. Moreover, because they are arranged in an orderly manner, they can arouse interest among viewers with artistic appreciation abilities. For example, porcelains from various kilns from the Song dynasty to the Qing dynasty, and ancient paintings from the Tang dynasty to the Qing dynasty, are systematically introduced. A long article will be released soon by the preview exhibition to provide a detailed report and explanation to the people. As for the National Games, there was a resolution to hold them every two years, rotating between the capital and various provinces and cities. This year's games will be held in Shanghai on Double Ten Day. The preparatory committee has decided to hold a meeting at the municipal government on the 8th of this month, but the specific plan will depend on the standing committee. When the Central News Agency asked about the Ministry of Education's recent plans, Minister Wang replied that the Ministry is currently striving to promote compulsory elementary education. Whether it can be realized depends on whether the government has a solution for the funds required for this plan.

Ministry of Foreign Affairs Replies to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Regarding the Request to Negotiate with the United States to Increase Egg Taxes; Minister to the United States has already negotiated with the U.S. State Department 141

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, previously based on a letter from the Egg Industry Association, stated that since Chinese eggs have been subject to heavy taxes by the United States, the export of fresh eggs to the United States has been cut off for many years. Only a small number of dried eggs and egg products have been shipped in recent times. Unexpectedly, the U.S. Congress has recently proposed to increase the sales tax on eggs. The severity of the tax rate is unprecedented. The selling price of dried egg white is approximately US$0.50 per pound, with the original tax being US$0.27. Now it needs to be increased by another US$0.31, making the total tax US$0.58, taxing over 100% of the value of the goods. The selling price of dried egg yolk is approximately US$0.14 per pound, with the original tax being US$0.27. Now it needs to be increased by another US$0.31, making the total tax US$0.58, taxing over 400% of the value of the goods. The selling price of frozen wet eggs is approximately US$0.11 per pound, with the original tax being US$0.11. Now it needs to be increased by another US$0.15, making the total tax US$0.26, which is approximately 200% of the value of the goods. This heavy tax by the United States will completely prohibit the import of Chinese eggs. Please forward to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to urgently telegram Minister Shi in the United States to protest and withdraw this unreasonable proposal. The Association sent a telegram to both the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Finance on the 26th of last month and received a reply from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs yesterday. The original text is recorded below: "Your telegram is noted. The Ministry has previously telegraphed Minister to the United States, stating that negotiations have been made with the U.S. State Department. Later, a telegram was sent urging a thorough negotiation. Now, according to your telegram, a reply is hereby issued for your information. This approval."

The Cotton Merchants of Three Provinces Continue to Petition for Increased Taxes on Foreign Cotton 143

Zhang Yuwen, Geng Zijing, Yang Yizhai, Guo Lizhai, Jie Qingxuan, Mao Tingfang, Sun Ruitang, Xiong Zhifu, Yi Qing, Guo Pinsan, Cao Shaoling, Gao Ziming, Yang Ruitian, Zhang Jifu, Wang Ziming, Li Libo, Wang Zizhong, and other representatives of cotton merchants from Shanxi, Shaanxi, and Henan provinces submitted a document to the National Government, the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, the Legislative Yuan, and the Cotton Control Committee on March 31st, stating (abbreviated titles):

We respectfully submit this petition concerning the unbearable pressure from foreign cotton, humbly requesting increased taxes to curb it. Merchants and the public alike observe the current situation where foreign cotton floods the market, is recklessly dumped, and Chinese cotton sales are entirely usurped, causing enormous losses and a dire situation urgently requiring relief. We preemptively telegraphed a major portion of this matter to your departments on the 23rd of this month, requesting that increased taxes be imposed to curb it.

It is our understanding that the purpose of tariffs is to regulate the import of foreign goods and to protect the sale of domestic products, and especially to prevent foreign goods from undercutting and suppressing domestic products, which is its primary objective. In the past, our national tariffs were constrained by foreign powers, lacking the freedom to increase them, and merely served as a source of national revenue. Its original purpose was almost entirely lost. Moreover, the tax rates were lower than those of any other country, which allowed foreign merchants to bring in their surplus products in vast quantities, like water flowing downhill, surging and sweeping away our hard-earned money by the tens and hundreds of millions. The decline of our national power and the exhaustion of our people's strength are mainly due to this.

Our National Government, recognizing this, strives to fight and resolutely declares tariff autonomy. Decades of restraint are lifted at once, and all people rejoice and congratulate each other. However, given that autonomy is just beginning, some reservations are unavoidable, and a gradual increase method is adopted to show prudence. Therefore, the fundamental purpose of tariffs to curb the undercutting of foreign goods has not yet been fully realized. This matter concerns the national economy, and merchants and the public dare not add frivolous opinions. However, foreign merchants have superior financial resources and their ambition toward our vast market is growing. The previous tax increases were minimal and only slightly restrained them, while our merchants and the public, suffering from years of floods and droughts, barely surviving, are still unable to compete.

Taking the cotton industry as an example, there are no fewer than a thousand cotton merchants in Shanxi, Shaanxi, Henan, Shandong, Shanghai, and other places, with businesses worth tens of millions. However, they are all scattered in their operations, with only enough capital to purchase goods and not enough to cover transportation costs, let alone the financial resources to stockpile and wait for sales. Therefore, every time goods are transported to a place, they must immediately borrow from banks to ensure turnover and then seek sales. As for foreign cotton merchants, they are all large corporations with deep roots. Economic aggression has long been their way of doing things. Our country's foreign cotton tax rate has always been low, making imports very convenient and sales very easy. Over the years, their accumulated power has become extremely strong, allowing them to toy with our merchants at will.

Therefore, at times, foreign cotton floods the market, creating a monopolistic image. When Chinese cotton comes on the market, they recklessly dump and do everything possible to suppress it, preventing people from buying Chinese cotton and making it impossible to sell. Cotton merchants are unable to repay their bank loans and are eventually forced to sell at low prices, with the proceeds used to repay the loans, often leaving them short. Cotton merchants are defeated, which inevitably affects farmers. The annual losses are incalculable, and the cumulative effect has led to the fragile situation of cotton merchants today. It is painful to talk about.

The reason for this is that foreign cotton exploits our country's low tariffs to manipulate prices at any time, employing its toxic strategy of undercutting and suppressing Chinese cotton. The way to save the industry is to address the symptoms and prescribe the right medicine, striking at the root of the problem, and increasing the foreign cotton tax heavily. Unless this is done, all other efforts will be in vain. Because if the tax is heavy, the quantity imported will inevitably decrease, and their toxic plan of undercutting will also be limited by the increased cost, preventing them from implementing it fully. Our dying cotton industry's hope for recovery lies in this.

Furthermore, we are an agricultural country, and cotton is a major agricultural product, with the Northwest being its production area. In recent years, the National Government has been developing the Northwest and striving to improve cotton quality and increase production. Farmers are then compared to improvements in quality and increased production. Farmers then compared to each other. They managed to improve their operations more and more each day with greatly increased production. It is estimated that it already meets our national needs. We can no longer purchase foreign cotton and plug this hole. Compared to the past, we should have been rejoicing. How could we know that, despite our efforts to transport and sell, we cannot escape the undercutting and suppression of foreign cotton, either becoming stagnant and unable to sell, or being forced to suffer unbearable losses, ultimately causing those of our people who are trying their best to retreat in defeat? The reason the National Government is developing the Northwest, taking cotton as an example, is that while it intends to love us, it is actually harming us. This is certainly not the original intention of our government to benefit the country and the people.

Merchants and others are suffering losses now, and the situation is critical. We humbly beg your department to understand the situation, overcome all difficulties, and immediately increase the import tax rate on foreign cotton. We also request you to grant and implement this measure to provide relief and alleviate the difficulties of merchants. We urgently submit this petition, hoping that you will consider it.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Maritime Vessel Runs Aground Outside Zhenhai; Fully Loaded with Saigon Rice; Awaiting High Tide for Rescue 146

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's leased merchant vessel Maritime, weighing 3,000 tons, previously sailed to Lao Yao and recently changed its course to Annam to load Saigon rice for unloading in Ningbo. On the 4th of this month, the vessel, fully loaded with rice, sailed to the sea off Hudun Mountain outside Zhenhai, more than ten nautical miles from Zhenhai. Due to mistakenly navigating the wrong channel, it ran aground on the shallows near Hudun Mountain. At the time, the captain measured the water depth, which was less than sixteen feet, while the Maritime vessel had a draft of more than twenty feet. With the heavy load, the hull sank five feet deep into the sand. After running aground, the captain tried to speed up the engine to escape, but the bottom of the vessel was deeply embedded in the sand, making it impossible to move. He had no choice but to telegraph the Shanghai headquarters yesterday morning. Upon receiving the report, the headquarters notified the shipowners of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and had the chief shipowner telegraphed the Xinjiangtian vessel of Ningbo, requesting it to pay attention when passing through the waters off Hudun Mountain to avoid running aground. The Maritime vessel is currently awaiting high tide. If it can escape danger, that would be best; otherwise, a tugboat will need to be dispatched for rescue.

In the case of Western officer Niu Men of the Longhe vessel, who forced and beat seaman Tong Tianhou of the Xianghe vessel, causing him to fall into the water and die, the Chinese Seamen's Union sent secretaries Zhao Banfu and Sun Lyping to handle the negotiations for this case. The Ningbo Fellow-Villagers Association Concerns Itself with the People's Food in Their Hometown; 50,000 Shi of Tax-Exempt Foreign Rice to be Distributed to Counties in Old Ningbo Prefecture 150

Due to the drought in Zhejiang Province last year, all counties in Ningbo Prefecture were affected by the disaster. Reports of crop failures were received from various places. During the transition from spring to winter, farmers already suffered from a shortage of food. As they prepared for spring plowing in this transitional period, the difficult situation in the countryside was even more unimaginable. After repeated discussions among the executive and supervisory committee members, it was decided to request a tax-exempt passport from the Ministry of Finance to purchase 50,000 shi of foreign rice for distribution to the counties for disaster relief or price stabilization. The tax-exempt passport has now been received, and the purchase and distribution of rice are planned soon. The letter sent to the disaster relief sub-committees of the county governments is recorded below:

"Greetings. Last year's drought in Zhejiang Province severely affected all counties in Ningbo Prefecture. However, the provincial government's investigation of the disaster and handling of winter and spring relief efforts did not include the counties, leaving the disaster victims in Ningbo Prefecture feeling left out. The members of our association, due to our hometown ties, could not bear to stand idly by. Therefore, amid the impossibility of finding other methods, we separately planned a relief method. We sent a letter to the Shanghai Jiaxu Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association, which forwarded it to the Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association, requesting a tax-exempt passport from the Ministry of Finance to purchase 50,000 shi of foreign rice. We have now received it. This tax-exempt foreign rice is Western Rice No. 2. Because it is exempt from import tax, the price per shi can be reduced by several yuan compared to the current market price. We plan to distribute the entire 50,000 shi to the counties of Ningbo Prefecture, so that each county can prepare funds to transport and distribute it separately for disaster relief or price stabilization, hoping that the disaster victims can benefit somewhat. The amount of rice allocated to your county is approximately so many shi. We would like your government's disaster relief sub-committee to quickly raise the funds and send representatives to Shanghai to contact and transport the rice. This matter concerns disaster relief, so we hope you will investigate and expedite the process and reply accordingly."

The Lawyers Association Issued Three Notices to All Members Yesterday 151

The Shanghai Lawyers Association issued notices to all members yesterday, which are recorded below:

(1) Calling for a General Meeting to Re-elect Staff. We respectfully inform you that the Spring General Meeting of Members will be held at 2:00 p.m. on the 28th of this month (Sunday) at the Hushi Club, located at the intersection of Guizhou Road and Beijing Road. The meeting will report on association affairs and re-elect staff. In addition to publishing a notice in the newspaper, we are sending this letter accordingly. We hope that your esteemed members will take note and attend the meeting on time to deliberate. Furthermore, all members who have not paid their regular fees for more than four months and have not paid after being urged by letter are required to pay their outstanding fees by the 14th of this month. After the deadline, we will report their withdrawal from the association in order to calculate the statutory number of attendees for the meeting. This is a combined notice. We wish you peace.

(2) "The Ministry of Law Approves the Committee System." We respectfully inform you that this association previously received an order from the Shanghai Local Court, forwarded from Order No. 3517 of the Ministry of Judicial Administration, based on a request from the China Rule of Law Society. The request stated that the Shanghai Lawyers Association uses a committee system, which is inconsistent with Article 26 of the Lawyers Regulations, and requested that we comply with the regulations. The Shanghai Lawyers Association was previously granted permission to implement the committee system due to special circumstances. Since it was a temporary expedient, it should still follow Article 26 of the Lawyers Regulations and be amended accordingly. After receiving this order, this association convened a series of general meetings of members to discuss the association's rules. However, the meetings were adjourned due to insufficient attendance. Later, based on a proposal from members Wu Guochang and 21 others, it was noted that since this association was granted permission to implement the committee system eight years ago, its work efficiency has actually been higher and its affairs have progressed more smoothly than during the chairman system. In terms of re-electing staff each term, there are fewer adjournments. In contrast, associations using the chairman system often adjourn re-elections repeatedly, even convening them for several years without successful re-elections. The large size of this association is unmatched by other associations, and the special circumstances justifying the use of the committee system still exist. Since receiving the order to amend the association's rules, seven meetings have been held without any success. The sentiment of the people can be gauged. Please forward the proposal of over 170 members to maintain the temporary association's rules regarding the provisions of the committee system to the Ministry of Judicial Administration for consideration. This was approved by the 191st joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committees of this association and forwarded to the Ministry of Judicial Administration for instruction. Later, we received Approval No. 841 from the Ministry of Judicial Administration, which stated, "The report and proposal are noted. Since Shanghai has special circumstances, the committee system may be temporarily used before the Lawyers Law is formulated. A copy is kept on file." This was approved by the 193rd joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committees of this association and should be forwarded to all members for their information and record. We are sending this letter accordingly. We hope you will take note.

(3) "Change in the Authority of Land Agents." We respectfully inform you that, based on a previous letter from member Hu Fenglian requesting a transfer of the letter to the Municipal Land Bureau to change the procedures for land sales and transfers and mortgage registrations, this association sent a letter to the Municipal Land Bureau requesting a change in procedures. If the individual cannot be present, their legal representative may be present to carry out the land sales and transfer and mortgage registration. Later, we received a reply from the Director of the Municipal Land Bureau, stating, "The Land Certificate Transfer and Registration Procedures and the Real Estate Mortgage Registration Rules approved for implementation in this city do not have provisions for agents. However, Article 68 of the Shanghai Land Law stipulates that when an agent applies for registration, an authorization letter should be attached. In the future, cases may be handled accordingly." This was approved by the 193rd joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committees of this association and should be forwarded to all members for their information and record. We are sending the attached reply letters accordingly (omitted). We hope you will take note and act accordingly.

Employee of the Mardy Company Sues for Theft After Car is Recovered 152

Ma Shiqi, residing at No. 1 Yuansheng Lane, No. 93 Pisani Road, French Concession, previously purchased a car from the Mardy Motor Company at No. 80 Avenue Edward VII, numbered 6886, priced at 4,700 taels. It was agreed that payments would be made in installments. If payments were overdue, the car would be repossessed. A contract was signed as evidence. Because Ma was overdue for three installments, totaling over 600 yuan, the foreman of the company ordered employees Feng Xiangsheng (37 years old, from Jiading, residing at No. 436 Rue du Pere Robert), Shu Shangli (27 years old, from Nanjing, residing at No. 2 Shenderi Lane, Daxi Road), Shi Wenyuan (14 years old, from Jiaxing, residing at No. 13 of a certain lane on Jing'an Temple Road), and Ling Renjie (24 years old, residing at an unknown address) to go to Ma's residence in Yuansheng Lane and tow the car back to the dealership. However, Ma's chauffeur, Meng Suilong, noticed them and apprehended and detained them, accusing them of theft. The next day, they were sent to the Second Special Court and charged with theft under Article 338 of the Criminal Code. After questioning, each was released on bail pending further investigation. Yesterday, they were summoned again. According to the plaintiff, Ma Shiqi, the defendants did not commit theft. They were employees of the Mardy Motor Company and it was a misunderstanding. He requested that they not be prosecuted. During the questioning, Li Xiangsheng and the others confessed that they were indeed ordered by the foreman of the company to recover the car and were not stealing. Attorney Olsen, representing the defendants, argued that the defendants were instructed by the foreman of the Mardy Motor Company to retrieve the car and were in a passive position. The charge of theft brought by the police is unfounded. The plaintiff also does not wish to prosecute because the police suspect that there are other issues involved, which is why the case was submitted. Even if there was negligence, the company should be held responsible. The defendants did not commit any crime and should be acquitted. Judge Sun Penghuan agreed and declared the debate closed. The verdict is scheduled to be announced at 10:00 a.m. on the 10th. The defendants remain on their original bail.

Municipal Social Affairs Bureau Sends Personnel to Visit Group Wedding Participants to See If They Can Practice Thrift and Not Indulge in Extravagance 154

The first New Life Group Wedding Ceremony in this city was held on the 3rd in the City Hall Auditorium. Details have been recorded in various newspapers. The Social Affairs Bureau has been paying close attention to whether the married couples are following the New Life methods and practicing thrift. Before the event, they inquired of each married couple. Of the 57 couples, 8 only held family banquets without entertaining guests. On the evening of the 3rd, the bureau sent Sun Yongyi, director of the Public Welfare Section, and staff members Yan Wenkai and Lei Kenan to randomly inspect 16 households and visit the banquet locations and new couples' homes. The survey results showed that 1 household had 1 table of wine, 2 households had 2 tables, 1 household had 3 tables, 4 households had 4 tables, 2 households had 5 tables, and 1 household each had 6, 7, and 8 tables. Only 1 household held a large banquet for guests, and 1 household had a public banquet hosted by friends. Most families were able to understand the meaning of the New Life movement and save unnecessary expenses. The Social Affairs Bureau expressed deep satisfaction with this. It is reported that in the future, the format of the "Wedding Notice" for participants will be specified, stating that there will be no pretense and no gifts will be accepted, so that all citizens can reduce the burden of social expenses and make further reforms to shift away from extravagance and vulgarity.

The case of Jushunyi Sauce Garden at 187 Ximen Road in the French Concession being cut off from electricity by the French Municipal Council due to an increased liquor tax has been appealed to the Municipal Association Branch and the Chinese Taxpayers' Association, but no solution has been found after ten days. The French Concession Chinese Taxpayers' Association yesterday sent separate letters to the French Municipal Council Chinese Directors Lu Bohong, Zhu Yanzhi, Zhang Xiaolin, Zhang Jixian, and Qi Yunqing, requesting them to seriously negotiate with the French authorities to uphold justice. The original letter is recorded as follows: To the Honorable Directors, upon investigation, the French Concession Municipal Council charges liquor taxes in three categories: seven yuan, three yuan eight jiao, and one yuan four jiao. Now, a five yuan category has been added, for a total of four categories. However, the Council does not consider the scope of business of the stores when collecting this liquor tax, but arbitrarily increases the tax. For example, the liquor tax for Jushunyi Sauce Garden, which is located in a remote area at 187 Ximen Road, Sapise Road, was 2 yuan 8 jiao last year. This year, without notice, it was suddenly increased to 5 yuan per month, and on March 25, the electricity was suddenly cut off due to non-payment of the tax. Although this matter is trivial, the Council's handling is unfair and using electricity cutoff as a weapon to oppress the people is inappropriate. Directors of the Shanghai Branch of the Kawah Bank Charged, Many Defendants Cannot Be Served, Whether the Trial Can Proceed as Scheduled is Undecided 159

The head office of the Kawah Savings Bank is located in Hong Kong, while Guangzhou and Shanghai are branches. On New Year's Day this year, the Hong Kong head office and the Guangdong branch simultaneously announced their closure. However, the Shanghai branch took no action after receiving the telegram and continued business as usual on January 4, after the three-day New Year's holiday, leading outsiders to believe that the branch had separated from the head office and was independent. As a result, many people sent money for storage on January 4. Little did they know that the branch was only hoping to attract more deposits by not immediately closing down. Although the result was still a declaration of closure on January 5, only extending the period by one day, the victims had increased to as many as eleven households, including Jiang Zhijia. They had obtained a huge amount of deposits of 3,896 yuan. This was because the eleven households, including Jiang, saw that the branch was still operating on January 4 and mistakenly believed that it would not perish with the head office. They all deposited their money. Unexpectedly, the closure was announced on the 5th, and they began to regret being deceived. Among these depositors, Jiang Zhijia held three promissory notes with a due date of January 10, totaling 1,530 yuan. The remaining ten households were all cash deposits. Therefore, only Jiang initially thought that he would not suffer any losses, because he had sent a letter to the liquidator of the branch, stating that the promissory notes did not need to be collected on his behalf. Even though he had notified them, it was too late, and the money had already been collected. As a result, the eleven depositors felt that Jiang had suffered the greatest loss. Now, Jiang, along with the other depositors, having investigated the responsible parties of the branch, including shareholders and Chairman Zhao Jinqing, shareholders and Counselors Li Yaobang, Zhang Danru, He [blank] Qiu, Deng Zhaozhen, Lin Zhizhou, Zhong Biao, shareholder and Supervisor Zhao Yaozhang, Huang Yougan, General Manager [blank] Xitian, Supervisor Zhang Xinei, Manager Bai Hongji, and Deputy Manager Shen Hegao, filed a lawsuit with the First Special District Court against the responsible parties, claiming that the plaintiffs' money was deposited in the branch on January 4 and that the defendants were jointly and severally liable for the savings deposits under the law, requesting a judgment ordering the defendants to jointly repay 3,896 yuan, plus statutory interest. The First Special Court has now scheduled the trial for this month on the 19th in the afternoon, but many of the defendants cannot be served because their addresses are unknown. Therefore, it is still unknown whether they can be summoned to court when the trial begins.
