Judgment on Li Guojie's Appeal, "Criminal Procedure" Sentenced to Imprisonment for One Year and Two Months, "Civil Procedure" to Compensate China Merchants Bureau 700,000 Taels 164

Li Guojie, the former general manager and chairman of the China Merchants Bureau, was initially sentenced by the Shanghai District Court in September of the previous year for embezzlement of 700,000 taels of silver to three years in prison for breach of trust. Li was not satisfied and appealed to the Jiangsu High Court for the second instance, which changed the sentence to three and a half years for embezzlement. Li was still not satisfied and appealed to the Supreme Court, which ordered a retrial. Because Li was chronically ill and feared inconvenience during travel, the High Court appointed Hu Shanhong, the chief judge of the Criminal Court, along with Judges Zhang Bingci and Zhang Zepu, and Prosecutors Hong Yu [blank], Shen Yuren, and Zhu Minghe, and two clerks, to come to Shanghai to conduct the trial at the First Tribunal of the Shanghai District Court. The trial concluded, and the date for sentencing was set for the 5th of this month. Yesterday was the scheduled date for sentencing. At 10 am, bailiff Chen Junfang and deputy bailiff Chen Xihui took a car to the Shanghai Hospital to bring Li Guojie to the court. The Public Security Bureau also sent Squad Leader Yu Ruhai of the Detective Squad and police officers to escort him in a car to ensure security. At 11 am, Hu Shanhong, the chief judge of the Criminal Court, along with the judges and prosecutors, took their seats in the First Tribunal and ordered Li Guojie to be brought to the dock. After briefly questioning his age and origin, Judge Hu rose and announced the judgment. In the case of Li Guojie's appeal for malfeasance, (main text) the original judgment regarding the crime of malfeasance is revoked. Li Guojie, with the intention of illegally possessing for himself, embezzled public property in his possession and is sentenced to imprisonment for one year and two months. The number of days detained before the judgment is finalized shall be credited at two days for one day of imprisonment. In the case of Li Guojie's appeal for civil suit for malfeasance, (main text) Li Guojie shall compensate the China Merchants Bureau 700,000 Shanghai guiyuan taels of silver, and shall pay interest at an annual rate of 8% from April 28 of the 22nd year of the Republic of China until the date of full repayment. If dissatisfied, he may appeal according to the law. After the judgment was completed, he was ordered to return Li to custody. Deputy bailiff Chen Xihui escorted Li into a car and drove him directly to Shanghai Hospital for custody pending further instructions.

Municipal Bureau of Public Works Arranges for the Construction of Ditches and Canals in the Southwest District of Huhang 165

Except for Lujia Hong Road and PuZhao Road, where main ditches have been constructed successively, the various roads east of Rihui Port in the southwest district of Shanghai rely on open ditches for drainage. Every time the summer and autumn seasons change, the low-lying areas retain polluted water, which is difficult to discharge, directly affecting the public health of citizens and indirectly harming the road surface. In view of this, the Municipal Bureau of Public Works, after being approved by the Municipal Government, is now arranging for the construction of main ditches in Xietu Road (from Manufacturing Bureau Road to Xiaomuqiao Road), Manufacturing Bureau Road (from Xieqiao to Longhua Road), Dapu Road (from Xietu Road to Xiexu Road), and Jumen Road (from Xiexu Road to Xietu Road). Work has now begun. After the project is completed, not only can the city appearance be expected to be tidy, but also the residents along the road who have been suffering from the inability to solve the drainage problem due to the lack of main ditch facilities can apply to the Road Engineering Management Office of the Municipal Bureau of Public Works on Zhonghua Road for connection to the ditch according to the regulations. This will benefit public health and is not a small matter.

Railroad Intermodal Coffin Transport Exempts Transfer Station Handling Fees, Effective April 21 166

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration received instructions from the Ministry of Railways yesterday to cancel the transfer station handling fees for intermodal coffin transport, effective April 21. The original order is recorded as follows: According to the Intermodal Transport Office's case submission, the 58th case "Request to Regulate Coolie Fees at Transfer Stations for Intermodal Coffins" and the 59th case "Handling Fees for Intermodal Coffins Urgently Need to Be Regulated" were discussed at the 17th Domestic Intermodal Transport Conference. The 236th resolution stated that "It is clearly specified that transfer stations will collect handling fees and river crossing fees when crossing rivers." The investigation shows that charging handling fees at transfer stations is inconsistent with the principles of intermodal transport. Therefore, there are no regulations for charging handling fees at transfer stations for intermodal goods, luggage, and packages. If only the handling fees at transfer stations for intermodal coffins are to be charged, they should all be waived. If there are river crossing fees to be charged, they should be collected by the originating station along with the freight. As for re-transfer station handling or re-packaging fees, they should not be charged to the coffin owner or escort. Except for those handled by long-term employees hired by the railway, the various railways should give coolie subsidies according to the circumstances. No matter the railway or the coolie, no fees may be charged en route. It is scheduled to be implemented from April 21 of this year. If any station coolies demand money, they should be strictly punished to maintain the discipline of the road. In addition to separate orders, this order is to be followed. (This Bureau has already forwarded it to the Transportation Department for compliance)

Yu Hezhenya, a Guangdong woman living in a foreign-style house at No. 60 Avenue Petain in the French Concession, was kidnapped by bandits in front of the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court on Avenue Petain at 8:30 AM on October 21 of last year and held for ransom. On November 19, detectives and inspectors of the French Police Station, Jin Jiulin, sent detectives Zhang Ziying, Zhou Buguang, Zhou Bingcheng, and Tao Ronglin to Suzhou to arrest suspects Li Shengxiao and Wang Fukang, a member of the gang who was negotiating the ransom. During the period of detention, the bandits showed a large leather suitcase and threatened to kill her if they did not pay the ransom in a few days and put her in the suitcase. The confessions were the same as the previous confessions. As a result, because the key criminal Wang Fukang was not present, it was decided to postpone the trial to the 19th for further interrogation, and the defendants remained in custody awaiting instructions.

The Reputation of Jiufu Company's Buliduo: Effective, Especially for Government Officials and Celebrities with Endorsements 185

Recently, the weather has been erratic, and there have been many colds and coughs. A considerable number of people have also had relapses of old illnesses such as lung disease and syphilis. These symptoms are effectively treated with Buliduo produced by Jiufu Company on Baker Road in Shanghai, with satisfactory results. As a result, medical and pharmaceutical circles are using it and the demand exceeds the supply. This shows how popular it is. Buliduo is originally produced in two types: Pure and Containing Guai. Pure Buliduo strengthens the body and treats the lungs and is effective for all types of weakness. Containing Guai also treats coughs, excessive phlegm, pulmonary tuberculosis, and tuberculosis. Since the settlement of the dispute with Pareto last year, three new types have been added: Containing Iodine, Containing Arsenic, and Containing Quinine. Containing Iodine specializes in treating asthma, scrofula, and all stages of syphilis. Containing Arsenic specializes in treating blood loss, weakness, and various skin diseases. Containing Quinine specializes in treating lack of energy and decreased appetite. All have great effects. Therefore, many government officials and celebrities have given endorsements, such as President of the Legislative Yuan Sun Ke's endorsement "Profound Merit for Helping the World", President of the Control Yuan Yu Youren's endorsement "Buliduo", President of the Examination Yuan Dai Chuanxian's endorsement "Buliduo", Chief of Shanghai Security Office Yang Hu's endorsement "Support Vitality", and former Shanghai Garrison Commander Dai Ji's endorsement "Improve Health". The reputation is so great.

Weather Report 193

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that Shandong's surroundings were partly cloudy and partly clear, with gentle and undefined winds. The middle and lower reaches of the Yangtze River were cloudy, with unsettled conditions and southeasterly winds, with morning fog. This was due to a low pressure system in northwestern China. The East China Sea and the Taiwan Strait were overcast with strong northeasterly winds. Typhoon Mindano, northeast by north, was stalling, with its center point at 6:00 AM approximately within 120 miles of 13 degrees north latitude and 130 degrees east longitude. Wind force unknown. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the local temperature was at its highest 63.34.0. On the same day last year, the highest temperature was 49.8 and the lowest 44.4.

Patrolling Police Arrest Five Bandits; Confess to Being the Murderers of Zhao Xianglin

Zhou Yida, chief of the Hejiajiao substation of the Xujiahui police station in western Shanghai, along with police officers Yang Youlu, Li Renhai, Li Wenbin, Gao Yuefeng, and others, were patrolling the Zhongshan Road Hongqiao area yesterday afternoon around 7:00 PM when they suddenly saw five people standing on the side of the road whispering to each other. Chief Zhou, seeing their suspicious behavior, was about to step forward to conduct a search when the group, feeling guilty, fled into the wheat fields. One of them, with a pockmarked face (namely Wang A'si), even dared to show a gun in resistance but was unexpectedly subdued by Yang Youlu and the six-inch live ammunition pistol, number 3980, was snatched away. The remaining four thieves, Zhou Jingsheng, Ding Qianhai, Shen Quan, and Chen Guilin, were chased all the way to the vicinity of Lujiazhai on the Fales Road before being apprehended one by one, with no one escaping. Flashlights, pills, pawn tickets, and other items were found on them. They were taken back to the station where, after strict interrogation by Director Hong Zhen, the thieves were exposed. According to Wang A'si's confession, he is 40 years old, from Wuxi, and lives in the workshop of the Yihua Yarn Factory in Yangshupu, working as a laborer. Yesterday, a foreman named Mr. Zhang and the five defendants opened room 17 of the Hongxiang Hotel in Nicheng Bridge to discuss fighting in Zhoujia Bridge. The gun was given to me by Mr. Zhang and was not for robbery. Today, after meeting the defendants and others on Zhongshan Road, I was arrested by the patrolling police. Zhou Quansheng confessed that he is 33 years old, from Changzhou, lives in a small inn, and makes a living as a laborer. Last night, he and the five defendants stayed in the Hongxiang Hotel. Wang A'si suggested robbing an old woman's house near a temple in western Shanghai. The gun belonged to Wang, and he asked me to meet him at the Wangjialou teahouse at 4 o'clock. Ding Qianhai confessed that he is 41 years old, from Changzhou, lives in Yishengli, Yangshupu, and works as a tailor. The rest of his confession was similar to Zhou Jingsheng's. Shen Longquan confessed that he is 32 years old, from Wuxi, lives at No. 34, Shen'anli, Tangshan Road, and works as a coppersmith in the Huatong Electric Factory. Last night, Wang A'si and the other five people opened a room in the Zhongshan Hotel in Lihong Bridge. Wang suggested robbing an old woman's sock factory on Zhongshan Road in western Shanghai. Wang had robbed it twice before. The gun was borrowed from Little Changzhou. The murderer who shot Zhao Xianglin was also them (referring to Wang and Little Changzhou). Chen Guilin confessed that he is 24 years old, from Wuxi, lives in Hengqingli, Beiler Road, and works as a vendor. The rest of his confession was the same as Zhou Jingsheng's. After hearing the confessions, Director Hong sent the five captured thieves, Wang A'si and others, along with the seized pistols and other items, to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for interrogation. Police Chief Zhou Yida and police officer Yang Youlu, and others bravely captured the thieves, were loyal to their duties, and requested the director to commend them.

Special Issue of the Second Fundraising Convention of the Chinese Anti-Tuberculosis Association

Declaration of the Fundraising Convention of the Chinese Anti-Tuberculosis Association 196

— Li Ting'an

The purpose of this association is solely to prevent and treat tuberculosis. It was established in October 1933. At that time, its trend was revealed; as for the methods of activity, in terms of prevention, we must awaken the people of the country to know the harm of tuberculosis attacks, obtain tuberculosis prevention knowledge, reform bad habits, and encourage each other, hoping to reduce tuberculosis and eradicate it; in terms of treatment, we must save the sick to restore health, which is also to prevent the spread of tuberculosis bacteria everywhere; in the past year, the matters that have been undertaken: one is to publish tuberculosis prevention magazines to impart tuberculosis prevention knowledge, the second is to hold summer children's health camps to enhance children's bodies and develop their tuberculosis prevention habits; the third is to set up the first and second tuberculosis clinics to provide free diagnosis and treatment for patients, but because of the prevalence of tuberculosis patients, the aforementioned undertakings are by no means effective, and we must strive for development. Furthermore, in view of the fact that the people of European and American countries have done their best for tuberculosis prevention work, those who suffered deeply from tuberculosis in the past have now been greatly reduced, and the greatest reason for their success is due to the meticulous organization of tuberculosis prevention groups and the enthusiastic support of the people in various places; how can the Chinese nation lag behind? After public deliberation, it was decided that: starting from April 6, 1935, we will widely solicit members to go to work together. The significance of soliciting membership is as follows:

1. The relationship on the ethnic front: About 1.6 million Chinese compatriots die from tuberculosis every year, and about 16 million people are infected. If we do not plan now, the situation will inevitably get worse year by year, which is the greatest scourge for the future of the nation. As a member of the nation, how can we not fulfill our responsibility?

2. The relationship on the national front: Because Chinese people are subjected to the aforementioned tuberculosis attacks, their physical strength is weakened, and the national power is declining. The disaster of destruction is imminent. As a member of the country, how can we not fulfill our responsibility!

3. The relationship on the socio-economic front: The cost of a person who dies of tuberculosis, from birth to burial, is about 1,500 yuan per person. If 1.6 million people die each year, then our entire socio-economic system will lose 2.4 billion yuan annually. The number is already alarming, and 16 million tuberculosis patients who cannot work can possibly increase the productive forces of the socio-economy, but instead become the socio-economy's waste. The loss to the entire socio-economy is difficult to calculate. Therefore, the socio-economic loss in our country due to tuberculosis is at least tens of billions of yuan each year. Assisting in tuberculosis prevention is enough to maintain the socio-economy, which is also to reduce one's own direct or indirect losses. As a member of society, how can we not fulfill our responsibility!

4. The relationship on the front of human morality: If we occasionally see any animal injured or sick and in pain, we will inevitably feel compassion. Now that we know that 1.6 million people die from tuberculosis every year, and 16 million people are trapped in tuberculosis, we must also think of the loneliness of the orphans of the deceased and the anxiety of the families of the sick. How is their sorrow and suffering! In terms of human morality, how can we not fulfill our responsibility!

Some may say that the significance of joining the association is as mentioned, but what is the actual effect on tuberculosis prevention? The answer is: the more like-minded people there are, the greater the effect will be. Success can be achieved, without waiting for hesitation. If you do not believe me, please check the course of the reduction of the tuberculosis rate and tuberculosis mortality rate in various countries, and you will know that the expectation of this association is not false. Compatriots, gentlemen, why not come? This declaration is all.

A Letter Respectfully Informing Leaders from All Walks of Life in the Country to Participate in Tuberculosis Prevention 197

— Yan Fuqing

Chinese people often regard minor illnesses as unworthy of attention, and many people unknowingly lose their lives because of this. This kind of view is enough to mislead oneself and others, and it is enough to affect the national economy and the people's livelihood. Without mentioning other things, please take tuberculosis as an example; the entry of tuberculosis into the human body starts gradually, and the patient does not realize it, or thinks it is wind and cold, neglects treatment, or thinks it is hot and rashly uses coolants, so that 1.6 million people are sent to their deaths by it every year. These 1.6 million people are all young and productive members of society, and the direct and indirect impact on the country's population and economy cannot be calculated in quantity: not only that, but also those who transmit it to their children, called childhood tuberculosis, and those who linger in bed for more than 40 years and never recover, called lifelong tuberculosis. Just imagine how many people are neither alive nor dead? Speaking of it is truly alarming! According to reports from various sources: this disease accounts for 4,000 out of every 100,000 people. China's population is 400 million, so there are 16 million people in the country. This 16 million tuberculosis experts spread it to each other, increasing year by year, so our entire nation will not be destroyed by others, and we will not be able to survive in the world. Just imagine what a terrible and tragic thing this is!

In view of this, the Chinese Anti-Tuberculosis Association was established in October 1933 by uniting comrades from all walks of life. The purpose is to awaken the Chinese people to the seriousness of tuberculosis, to pay attention to it, to prevent it, and to resist it; and to give those who are already ill practical remedial treatment and guide them in the methods of health preservation. Since its establishment, although the time is very short, the work that has been done is fortunately also slightly scaled (see the work report of this association). At the time of the annual meeting, reviewing the past and encouraging the future, we feel even more that the tuberculosis prevention cause is of great importance to the national population and economy. In order to implement the original intention and improve the health of the nation, a three-year plan has been drawn up to promote it step by step and realize it as soon as possible. However, this matter is of great importance and cannot be achieved by the strength of a few people. I hope that leaders from all walks of life will call out loudly, so that all the mountains will respond, and the masses will work together to achieve this great event. I think those who care about the people will be happy to support it.

A Review of the Association's Establishment and One Year of Work 198

— Zhang Junjun

This association was jointly initiated by Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng, who contacted leaders from Chinese and foreign circles, as well as giants in the medical field. The inaugural meeting was held at the municipal government reception office on Xiafei Road on October 22nd of the 22nd year of the Republic of China (1933). Over 250 people attended, including Wu Tiecheng, Kong Xianxi, Wang Xiaolai, Liu Hongsheng, Niu Huisheng, Li Ting'an, and Xu Shiying. Wu Tiecheng delivered a speech, the gist of which was: The harm of tuberculosis is well known. In our country, approximately 1.6 million people die from this disease each year, and nearly 10 million are affected. Moreover, the majority are young, productive members of society, which has a very significant impact on the social economy! Fifty years ago, the prevalence of tuberculosis in many European and American countries was not much different from that in our country. However, due to effective prevention methods, the mortality rate from tuberculosis plummeted. For example, in England in 1875, the tuberculosis mortality rate was slightly less than 300 per 100,000, but now it has dropped to around 70. This is evidence of the effectiveness of tuberculosis prevention. According to surveys, the mortality rate in our country is more than six times higher than that in England, and as many as 40% of children under the age of fourteen are infected. If we do not take active preventive measures, what will become of the nation and the people? For this reason, I have specially contacted famous Chinese and foreign figures in Shanghai, as well as giants in the medical field, to jointly initiate the Chinese Anti-Tuberculosis Association, to plan preventive measures, so as to strengthen the physique of the nation. However, this matter is very important. It is not easy to achieve results without collective efforts, step-by-step planning, and a sound organization. Now that we have the enthusiastic participation of leaders from all walks of life, the future development of this association will surely be limitless. After Wu Tiecheng finished his speech, the various ongoing matters and membership types were discussed. It was resolved that anyone who wishes to join the association can become a member, regardless of gender or nationality. The categories are divided into two types: (1) Group members, limited to legal organizations; (2) Individual members, divided into four types: ordinary members, sustaining members, permanent members, and student members. Subsequently, honorary presidents, executive directors, supervisors, and directors were elected. Wu Tiecheng was elected as honorary president, Madame Liu Ruiheng Kong Yongzhi, Wang Xiaolai, Yu Qiaqing, and Xu Xinliu as honorary vice presidents, Niu Huisheng as chairman, and Li Ting'an as vice chairman. Zhu Hengbi, Yan Fuqing, Wu Liande, Wu Tiecheng, Bu Mei, Madame Xiao Zhiji, and J.A. Snell were elected as executive directors. Du Yuesheng, Ding Fubao, Liang Xiaochu, Lu Bohong, Shi Liangcai, Cai Xiangsun, Pang Jingzhou, and Chu Minyi were elected as supervisors. Liu Hongsheng and Kuang Fuzhuo. Lu Ganchen, Huang Renzhi, Lin Kanghou, Gu Yuqi, Zhu Qinglan, Wu Yun Chu, Ding Shujing, Li Denghui, Xu Jianping, Guo Shun, Xu Shiying, Dong Xian Guang, Hu Yunqiu, Pan Gongzhan, Li Zuwei, Jin Shuchu, Lu Yongchun, Diao Xinde, Chen Zhifang, Chen Wanli, Li Dachao, Tan Shixin, Wang Shuzhen, He Chichang, Jin Baoshan, Liu Wang Liming, Wu Xingya, Wang Xiaoying, Hu Xuanming, Song Guobin, Qian Muhan, J. Raberf S.M. Gurn. G.R. Fitcb C.M. Van Allen. J. H. Jordan. E. C. Lobenstin and others were elected as directors. All of the above was handled by Mr. Yang Huaiseng, an executive of the National Youth Association. Mr. Yang has always been very enthusiastic about public affairs. Since taking office as temporary executive secretary, he has planned everything and proceeded in various ways, which has begun to take shape. The above is the process of the establishment of this association. Now, the general situation of the association's work over the past year is described below:

(1) Re-employment of Staff: On December 14th of the 22nd year of the Republic of China (1933), Mr. Zhang Junjun was hired as the executive director of the association, and Mr. Li Chaozhang and others were hired to assist in all matters. Mr. Yang immediately handed over the various affairs to Mr. Zhang and Mr. Li to be responsible for. After the staff was hired, the work began to proceed. (2) Holding the First Membership Drive: On the evening of December 15th of the same year, a public banquet was held at the Hong Kong Road Bankers' Association to entertain leaders from all walks of life, and the first membership drive was held. More than 80 people, including male and female captains and persons in charge of the association, such as Zhang Junjun and Li Chaozhang, were immediately appointed. The captains proceeded separately with enthusiasm to introduce the association, and the number of people who joined was very enthusiastic, and the result was quite impressive. (3) Reception for the Press: At 4:00 p.m. on January 12th, the local press was invited to the Eight Immortals Bridge Youth Association, and an anti-tuberculosis film was shown. Those who attended included Li Ting'an, Director of the Bureau of Health, Yan Fuqing, President of the Red Cross Hospital, Li Dachao, Section Chief of the Municipal Government, and more than 40 reporters from various newspapers. Chairman Yan delivered a speech first, followed by a speech by Li Ting'an. Finally, there was a tea party, and educational films on tuberculosis prevention were shown, which explained the growth and treatment of tuberculosis bacteria in great detail. It was not until about 6:00 p.m. that everyone dispersed happily.

(4) Reception for Church Leaders: At 4:00 p.m. on January 19th, a meeting of church leaders was held at the association. Those who attended included Ting'an, Lai Douyan, Zhu Hengbi, Zhang Wei, Tian Cuibin, and Tu Baoluo. Li Ting'an, the chairman, delivered the opening remarks, followed by speeches by Dr. Lai Douyan and Zhang Wei, which stated that the number of people suffering from tuberculosis in China is the highest in the world, and the loss of talent and the waste of treatment are far greater than the annual civil war. We should pay close attention to public and personal hygiene to prevent tuberculosis from spreading further. Zhang Junjun then reported on the association's affairs, followed by a tea party, and Wu Zengui of Kodak Company screened anti-tuberculosis films. The meeting adjourned at about 6:00 p.m.

(5) Anti-Tuberculosis Broadcasting and Lectures: From January to March, President Yan Fuqing, Director Li Ting'an, Principal Weng Zhilong, Dr. Bu Mei, Dr. Zhang Wei, and Zhang Junjun were successively invited to the Gospel Broadcasting Station to give lectures on methods of preventing and treating tuberculosis. The active publicity was well received by the citizens. In the winter of last year, experts were continuously invited to give lectures, and staff were sent to major middle schools to promote national health and methods of preventing tuberculosis. According to statistics, there were 50 lectures last year, with approximately 100 to 1,200 listeners each time, which shows the attention paid to the issue of tuberculosis by all parties.

(6) Holding a Fundraising Campaign: On March 15th, Wu Tiecheng, Honorary President of the Association, hosted a banquet for celebrities from all walks of life in the city, and at the same time held a fundraising campaign, which was very successful. Mr. Chiang Kai-shek, Mr. Wen Lanting, Mr. Du Yuesheng, Mr. Shi Liangcai, Mr. Liu Zhi and others all enthusiastically donated to promote the realization of the association's cause. Their spirit of serving the public is truly commendable. In addition, donations were widely solicited from celebrities, directors, and groups, and a total of 21,895.92 yuan was received in donations and membership fees, which enabled the association's work to be gradually realized. (7) Establishing a Tuberculosis Clinic: In order to meet the needs of society and promote the health of the people, the association established the first tuberculosis clinic at No. 306 Xilin Road, on the corner of Ximen Fangxie Road, on June 14th. In order to reduce the burden on the people and fulfill the mission of charitable relief, no consultation fees or medicine fees are charged. Since its establishment, the number of citizens who have visited the clinic for treatment by the end of December is 293 for initial consultations and 634 for follow-up consultations. This shows the prevalence of tuberculosis among the citizens.

(8) Nurses Visiting Patients' Homes: Since the establishment of the first clinic, the association hired Ms. Zhu Xiaopei and Shen Zongying to work as nurses. Every morning, they visited patients' homes separately to tell them about methods of prevention and treatment. After this news was released, patients' families requested nurses to visit them one after another. The seriousness of the tuberculosis problem is truly chilling!

(9) Holding a Children's Health Camp: In mid-June, the association prepared for a summer children's health camp. Later, the Education Bureau, the Health Bureau, the Children's Welfare Association, and the Chen Bao Newspaper all requested to join in the joint organization. Therefore, the five groups prepared to open the camp on July 6th. A total of 60 boys and girls registered to join. The general situation of the process and daily life have already been announced in the newspapers and published in the association's Anti-Tuberculosis Magazine, so I will not repeat them here.

(10) The Association's Work in the 13th Shanghai Municipal Health Campaign: The 13th Shanghai Municipal Health Campaign began on June 19th of last year. The association belonged to the Anti-Tuberculosis Group, so it carried out a large-scale anti-tuberculosis publicity campaign. It was planned that during the one week of the conference, leaders and celebrities from all walks of life in the city would be invited to give lectures on tuberculosis prevention. Every time a lecture was given, there were 500 to 600 enthusiastic listeners, which was unprecedented. Prior to the event, the association also sent letters to various hospitals in the city and the Shanghai Medical Association, requesting them to ask registered physicians to provide free physical examinations for citizens and half-price X-rays, all of which were accepted. A large number of people visited the physicians for treatment every day, and the hospitals, such as the Shanghai Plague Hospital, Guangren Hospital, Chinese Red Cross Hospital, and Sacred Heart Hospital, were so busy with physical examinations and X-rays that they could barely keep up.

(11) The Association's Book Donation: The association has prepared three books by Ding Fubao: "Guide to Lung Disease," "Lung Disease Treatment," and "Lung Disease Prevention," totaling more than 1,900 copies. The donation began on January 5th of last year. Because the books are rich in content, covering all aspects of tuberculosis prevention, treatment, and the common knowledge that patients should have, after the news spread, requests for the books poured in, and more than 1,800 copies were donated by the end of December. The large number of people suffering from the disease in the country can be seen from this. There are still some copies of the book remaining.

(12) Publication of the Anti-Tuberculosis Magazine: In order to popularize tuberculosis prevention education, the association has been preparing for several times, and the Anti-Tuberculosis Magazine was launched on November 1st. Mr. Kong Yongzhi, Wang Shijie, Chen Gongbo, Huang Shaoxiong, Liu Ruiheng and other gentlemen wrote inscriptions in support. In addition, the giants of the medical community across the country served as special editors. After the publication, it was warmly loved by all walks of life, and subscriptions poured in. The association is ashamed to receive this support and will continue to work hard to live up to the expectations of all parties. (13) Tuberculosis Vaccine Testing: Dr. Tang Shinian of the First Clinic is responsible for carrying out tuberculosis vaccine testing. Because tuberculosis is most likely to occur in children, in order to understand the prevalence of tuberculosis in China, it is necessary to carry out this academic test. The tuberculin reaction test (vaccine test) was performed on 385 students at Shanghai Middle School and Experimental Primary School, aged between 5 and 16. The method used was the Manfaux Intwcutaneous Method, and the dose used was O.T.roooo6 Gm. The results of the test on the 385 people are listed below:

Total Number Positive Reaction Negative Reaction Percentage of Positive Reactions

Under 5 years old 3 1 2 33.30%

6 to 10 years old 180 98 82 54.40%

11 to 15 years old 194 152 42 78.35%

Over 16 years old 5 4 1 80.00%

Although the number of people tested in the above table is small and is not enough to draw a conclusion, the phenomenon of school-age children showing a positive reaction to the tuberculin test indicates that the number of tuberculosis bacteria invading the body gradually increases with age. This is consistent with the results obtained by the Red Cross Society Gao Yishi in recent years. Few adults over the age of 20 are not invaded by tuberculosis bacteria. (14) Opening of the Second Clinic: In view of the large number of tuberculosis patients and the fact that Shanghai has a vast area and a large population, and the existing hospitals are not enough to meet the demand, the association is planning everything and actively adding tuberculosis clinics to benefit the citizens. The Third Clinic officially opened on April 2nd. The address is in Nanshi (15) Purchasing X-ray Machine with Huge Sum of Money: In order to facilitate the treatment of tuberculosis, the latest X-ray machine was ordered from the United States at a cost of 5,000 yuan in national currency. The machine is for the use of the Second Clinic. Patients who wish to be examined and photographed can go directly to the Shanghai Hospital Association Second Clinic for contact. (16) The Association's Hopes: Whether the work of tuberculosis prevention can be developed and whether the progress can be smooth depends on the amount of economic capacity. The association's various tasks are in active progress, but they are limited by economics and many have not been realized. It is hoped that enthusiastic people from all walks of life will enthusiastically donate, either as members or by soliciting donations on behalf of the association, so that the association's cause will thrive and the work of tuberculosis prevention will spread throughout the country. This will not only be a blessing for the future of the nation, but the association will also be honored.

Free Talk

Leisure 199

— Tang Tao

Yinxi, the Prince Shen of the Qing Dynasty, was very good at writing poetry. He once wrote a woodcutter's song, which said:

No human voices heard, only the sound of axes, the silent echo of the rocks, the startled birds flying away with a ding. Getting firewood to exchange for wine, returning drunk, stepping on the moon, singing mountain songs clearly; befriending wood and stone, without decline or glory, white clouds and flowing water from morning to evening, ten thousand mountains hazy with green smoke.

"Getting firewood to exchange for wine, returning drunk, stepping on the moon, singing mountain songs clearly; befriending wood and stone, without decline or glory," this is leisure, which is envied by many meat-eating friends. Yinxi, as a prince, loved elegance, letting his brother Yinzhen - Yongzheng - indulge in being emperor, suspicious, suppressing, and killing; while he traveled around mountains and rivers, wrote poetry and painted, acting as a carefree gentleman.

He wanted to enjoy leisure.

And he also bestowed this leisure on the woodcutter who "befriends wood and stone, without decline or glory." "Getting firewood to exchange for wine, returning drunk, stepping on the moon," the fortune is indeed very good, but this only expresses the leisure and elegance of talented scholars. In fact, the woodcutters who rely on two arms and an axe to chop wood in the mountains every day do not understand it. They only know about getting firewood to exchange for rice, and returning hungry, stepping on the moon. But if you were to say that, this would not be considered leisure, but rather a bit like hardship.

And hardship is not what elegant gentlemen enjoy talking about.

But it is still a fact that the woodcutters have no leisure to enjoy. Relying on a few poems and essays of leisure and elegance will not reverse the case in the end. The biggest evidence is the lack of money. Escaping the summer heat in Mount Lu and exploring the plum blossoms in Dengwei can also be considered leisure, but the woodcutters in Mount Lu still have to sweat, because they still have to work; the plum trees in Dengwei are only allowed to be admired, not chopped down. The casual interest of the elegant gentlemen shattered the rice bowls of the woodcutters who were holding axes.

Leisure has become the enemy of the poor in this way.

However, in Yongzheng's view, it was still worth promoting. He once changed the names of his brothers Yinxi and Yinsi to "Aqina" and "Seshei," "Aqina" meaning dog in Manchu, and "Seshei" meaning pig. These two, a dog and a pig, were imprisoned by Yongzheng for forming a party to plot rebellion, so that they could get rid of their worldly desires and enjoy some leisure.

Yinxi's watching flowers and admiring the moon, playing with antiques, and brewing good tea may be the so-called "sending sorrow to seclusion," but his leisure erases the facts before him, and he has long become a "Seshei" that is clear at a glance.

Poor Opera Troupe 200

— Long Gonggong

I once heard a ridiculous story about a poor opera troupe. The friends in the audience laughed until tears flowed out, because the story not only described the simplicity of a certain opera troupe, but also explained how the desires of the Chinese people are satisfied by what is supplied - which seems to explain something else as well.

The storyteller first introduced the fat female troupe leader. She was sitting at the entrance of the theater, with a large bamboo basket beside her; another male clerk stood on the other side of the entrance. The two of them held a straw rope in their hands. The audience threw two strings of cash into the bamboo basket, and they would lower the straw rope to let them in.

Secondly, he introduced the boots of the opera troupe. There was only one boot, and four characters had to show their right foot in front of the audience. This was naturally difficult. Therefore, the first one to walk had the natural right to enjoy the boots first. He walked to the stage, slowly kicked out one foot, and the boot was clearly revealed. Then he bent his foot backwards, and the second character who was about to come forward bent down to take off the boot for him - the people who heard this laughed.

He was talking about something that happened in a certain county in Sichuan. But anyone knows that this situation is common in China. Audiences everywhere show the same surprising degree of patience.

I also encountered a poor opera troupe in a small town in Guangdong. The actors were all elderly people. When the people in the town boasted that they had this group of old artists, they raised their thumbs and whispered: "Real beards and false teeth!" At other times, they would roar other praises: "Isn't it true that there are more officials than soldiers, more soldiers than guns, and more guns than bullets!"

A general walked out on the stage, presumably a commander-in-chief, shouting: "All the generals!" The four or five drummers next to him represented his subordinates and answered in unison: "Yes!" In fact, there was only one person acting. Later I learned that the good characters in the troupe refused to play soldiers, for fear of losing their status, and there were no bad characters.

When a young lady appeared on the stage without a bun, the drummers on the side would temporarily make a forced female response when she needed to be called.

In the past, the rules of Guangdong stage plays were that the performance had to continue until dawn. Before two or three o'clock, they performed the so-called wonderful part, and after that, it was a drag show. The people on the stage acted casually, and the people under the stage watched while dozing off, just waiting for dawn.

Once, after performing a play called "Shandong Outlaws" - which they called "the main attraction" - I saw a character who claimed to be an imperial envoy coming out from backstage to interrogate a female prisoner. There were no runners, no jailers, and not even a female prisoner. There was only a table, a gavel, and the imperial envoy himself on the stage.

The virtual female prisoner was probably the woman of a pirate who rebelled against the government, beautiful and full of integrity. The imperial envoy began by roaring and cursing her menacingly, saying that she "did not restrain herself and repeatedly troubled the heavens," threatening her with beheading; later, seeing that she was beautiful, he flirted with her with a smile, wanting to talk about love with her, with the warning that "obey me and live, disobey me and die." His fierce expression and love-making tactics sometimes seemed quite frightening. When dawn came, he didn't care whether the female prisoner was willing or not, and said to himself, "Now that it's dawn, the play has to be finished, you can come with me to the back room to sleep! Let's go."

Comedy 201

— Black Cherry

A deep night; there wasn't a sound on the street, making it seem unusually desolate. The northwest wind howled, and the police officer standing at the corner covered his ears with his collar, his legs trembling incessantly. The streetlights cast a pale light on the straight asphalt road. A whirlwind-like gust played with the weary people returning home, then vanished in an instant. Inside a 24-hour Cantonese restaurant, a few people were huddled around the stove, eating shrimp wontons, watching the desolate street, lacking the courage to step outside. A rickshaw was parked outside; the middle-aged driver stared blankly as the steaming wontons were delivered to others' mouths, suddenly feeling a pang of hunger himself, saliva welling up in the corner of his mouth, feeling extremely uncomfortable.

"Just staring at other people eating? You really are a bastard!"

Someone said this sarcastically. The bastard quickly swallowed his saliva and turned around to look for the speaker. All that was presented to him was a dark smile filled with contempt; the young man from Jiangbei, sitting on the rickshaw frame, held a half-smoked cigarette in his mouth, looking sly. He wanted to vent his anger on the young man, but he couldn't; he had to be patient.

"Damn it—" He didn't know who he was cursing.

At this moment, a rickshaw was being pulled toward them from afar. Sitting on the cushion was a ×× sailor, wearing a round hat and a navy uniform with a large collar. He propped up his legs and kicked the rickshaw driver in the back almost every two minutes. The rickshaw driver, biting his teeth, ran forward, the sound of his footsteps clearly echoing in the deep night, reaching everyone's ears. His heart was jumping, as if countless pebbles were rising and falling inside him, he thought he had met a devil tonight. He ran straight ahead—where on earth was this guy going? He seemed to have drunk a lot of alcohol; sometimes he muttered to himself; he never told the rickshaw driver where he wanted to go. He had been pulling for almost half an hour, running aimlessly, he really didn't know how it would end. Cold sweat broke out on his body; he was so anxious that he wanted to cry!

Suddenly, an unbearable kick landed on his back, almost knocking him onto the street; the sailor in the rickshaw, however, started yelling irritably, as if the rickshaw had done something wrong, shouting loudly. But no one could understand what he was yelling. At this time, the rickshaw was in front of the Cantonese restaurant, and some busybodies immediately left their wontons or raw fish congee and came out to watch the excitement. The unfortunate fellow who had been drooling because of his hunger and some of the rickshaw drivers also stood together, waiting for their companion to be humiliated by the ×× sailor until he cried.

The rickshaw stopped.

"Hey, what's going on!" the young man from Jiangbei asked. "He's crying! The ×× devil is still hitting him, this is outrageous!"

"Damn it!"

The ×× sailor used his fists and leather boots to beat the short, clumsy rickshaw driver, who didn't resist at all. The onlookers, however, had no sympathy, no righteous indignation, all standing there blankly as if they were watching a movie. The injured rickshaw driver looked at his compatriots with pleading eyes, begging for help; but no one gave him any reaction...

The shop assistant stood at the door, "Look, how interesting!" He even pulled the accountant from inside.

"You still say it's interesting! The rickshaw driver is already kneeling on the ground begging for mercy," the accountant said heavily, adjusting his nearsighted glasses.

Yes, the rickshaw driver did not resist after being humiliated, but instead begged for mercy. He knelt in front of the sailor in such a pitiful, servile manner, calling out in a low voice: "Master... ×× Great Master!... Spare my life!" Because he knew that the "Great Master" could even stab him to death, he was so scared that his face turned the color of green vegetables, begging for forgiveness in this way.

The ×× sailor, however, was satisfied and burst out laughing. Following the loud laughter like a waterfall, the audience also burst into laughter.

"Stupid thing, why don't you get up and run for your life?" Someone gently nudged the suffering man with his toe.

"Oh God..."

Crying out, he got up and quickly pulled the rickshaw away.

The police officer came over at this time and asked the onlookers, "What's going on?" However, no one answered him. Within three minutes, everyone had dispersed, some returning to the Cantonese restaurant to eat the half-bowl of raw fish congee left on the table; the young man from Jiangbei cursed the ×× devil, but he didn't dare to help the man who had just been humiliated. The victorious sailor rushed into a bar; the northwest wind was left blowing on the street, the streetlights shone coldly, and everything was as calm as if there had been no disturbance at all...

En Route 202

— Li Huiying

One of the Lake Tour Miscellanea

When I woke up in the morning, I was very happy, but when I looked at the heavily clouded sky, I was extremely disappointed; because in this kind of weather, it's not suitable to tour West Lake, and today was the scheduled day to depart for West Lake.

Regardless, I finally took my bedding and sat on a rickshaw to go to the station.

I've lived in Shanghai for five or six years, but I haven't been to West Lake yet. This is such a regrettable thing! Shanghai and West Lake are so close; not going to stroll around shows how lazy I am.

When I arrived at the station, the group of twenty-some people I was joining had already arrived. A group of students were jumping and bouncing, their joyful and eager state making it seem as if it would be good to arrive at West Lake immediately. They complained about the bad weather on the one hand, and on the other hand, they were afraid of rain. Fortunately, the rain hadn't started falling until after they boarded the train; instead, the sun bravely poked its head out after a while. Everyone was beaming with joy.

The train started, and with nothing to do, I opened a book of "Essays and Cartoons." I originally had a habit of preferring to look at the scenery along the way when riding the train, rather than reading books, even if it was just looking at plain fields and weeds; but this time, from the North Station all the way to Jiaxing, because I had traveled this route two or three times already, I was more familiar with the road, so I took a shortcut. I decided that I would look at the scenery outside the train window after the train passed Jiaxing.

Heaven didn't fulfill people's wishes. The sun had already been obscured by haze before the train even reached the Xinlonghua Station, and it even started drizzling after passing Jiaxing.

"How unlucky, it's actually starting to rain."

"Heaven really doesn't fulfill people's wishes, why does it deliberately make things difficult for people!"

"It's been raining for several days in a row, it should be clearing up, all it does is rain, endless rain!"

In the train carriage, some people were airing their grievances.

The weather gradually got colder, and I put on my cotton robe. I hadn't planned to bring this clothing in the morning, but I didn't expect that it would come in handy. The raindrops on the glass window slowly increased, obscuring my vision, and I couldn't see the scenery outside clearly.

Overall, I was lucky. Although the rain obscured the scenery outside the train window, there was something to spoil the scenery in the carriage: some students from Shanghai ×× College. They were putting on a civil drama without collecting tickets. Some of these college students were graduating (there was even a banner saying "Graduation Observation Group"?), and some, although they hadn't graduated yet, were all waiting to wear square caps. They deliberately made strange noises and exaggerated expressions, showing off their sex appeal. Because there were both men and women, the fun in the middle was even more pronounced, and good plays are never afraid of being continuous, people naturally want to watch, so it was very lively.

Looking at the group of middle school students sitting next to me, no, they were far behind, only able to watch others act stupidly, but unable to act themselves. This is probably due to a lack of ability. I secretly wished these middle school students watching the play would quickly improve, and after entering university, they could come to West Lake for a tour and perform a slapstick comedy in the carriage as well.

The rain fell harder and harder, no, denser, but not heavy, nor urgent. By the time we arrived in Hangzhou, it hadn't stopped yet. While getting off the train, I worried about touring the lake tomorrow. If only someone dared to guarantee that it would be sunny tomorrow, I would be willing to recite Amitabha Buddha ten times, I definitely wouldn't find it troublesome.

Our group of people got into rickshaws and headed towards the Girls' Middle School, which was our temporary lodging.

Farmer 203

— Ding Lang

Harsh winter suppressed their hunger, creditors temporarily lightened their footsteps; hoes drove away fatigue, once a year, it is spring again! The shimmering water threads through the fields, the fine rain awakens their life, the straw hats, the rain capes, filling them with excitement, the mud burying their legs, moving and moving searching for life. Hope permeates their hearts: 'Hope it won't be like last year's harvest'?

Mr. Juqing (8) 204

— Ke Ling

Although the principal is young, he has a very good idea: a strike. Wearing a pair of gold-rimmed tortoise-shell glasses, with a Western suit over his long robe, and leather shoes, he raised his voice, which had just broken, and delivered a passionate speech to the students: 'Everyone, children, go back and tell your families: Originally, we should have started classes a long time ago; but the former school director refused to hand over, there were no operating funds, so we had no choice but to not start classes! We should overthrow this... this... "reactionary element"!'

—Things were at a standstill.

In less than two or three days, this news spread throughout the town like an autumn wind. The students' fathers and elder brothers frowned; but the general tutors were enthusiastically inquiring about this matter everywhere, grinning as they listened to people talking, and then talking to other people about it.

Mr. Juqing also became a little excited. He didn't just feel the pleasure of watching a fire from across the river about this matter; he knew that if things escalated, it might have a positive impact on him. —In recent days, whenever it was time for school to let out in the evening, Mr. Juqing's triangular monkey face often appeared on the street.

This evening, Mr. Juqing was running along the East Street in the dim twilight, preparing to go see a friend to inquire about news. Suddenly, an old man wearing a blue cloth robe and a felt hat came towards him and greeted Mr. Juqing with a cupped fist:

"Oh, Mr.! How coincidental, I was just about to come visit you."

Hearing the voice, it was Soy Sauce Fu, the shopkeeper of Yuxing Soy Sauce Shop on East Street. He then grabbed Mr. Juqing's arm and ran into a small tavern.

A small plate of peanuts, a small plate of dried tofu, they sat down in the "private room" behind the dark "Qinglong Pi" liquor. Soy Sauce Fu said:

"Mr., do you know? My shop has been sealed by the school."

Mr. Juqing had just heard people talking about this news; but he made a very surprised expression: "Oh, why?"

Soy Sauce Fu coughed and told him: the shop of Yuxing is the property of the district-run elementary school, rented from the school. Last year, Chu Runfu, the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, was the school director, and he collected the rent for March this year; this year, Zhang Xiaofeng took office again, but he forced Fu to pay again, saying that it had already been paid to the former school director. There was no effect. The principal, without distinguishing right from wrong, said that they were intentionally delaying payment, undermining education. A letter was sent to the town's Public Security Bureau, and Yuxing Soy Sauce Shop was closed on the same day, sealed with a cross-shaped strip. —

Page 14

Educational News

All Schools Handling Boy Scouts Must Hire Full-Time Coaches, Ministry of Education Orders All Departments and Bureaus 205

(Nanjing, 5th) The Ministry of Education ordered all departments and bureaus, citing a letter from the General Association of the Boy Scouts of China, stating that most of the Boy Scout groups in various regions are run by schools, and there is no fixed funding. Most of them cannot hire full-time coaches. Some are staffed by physical education teachers, and some are randomly taught by ordinary teachers, resulting in many errors in academics and many disorders in discipline for the Boy Scouts. This is contrary to the original purpose of promoting the Boy Scout cause. Further investigation reveals that your ministry has already issued a general order to all junior high schools in the country to uniformly implement Boy Scout training, and Boy Scout funding has been included in the school budget. Now that funding is secured, hiring full-time coaches should be easy. Therefore, it is proposed that your ministry issue a general order to all schools that, in the future, all Boy Scouts must hire full-time coaches in order to increase efficiency, etc. Approved. Further investigation reveals that the implementation of Boy Scout training in junior high schools and Boy Scout equipment costs should be included in the school budget, as previously ordered by the Ministry in June of last year. All Boy Scout coaches in various schools should hire full-time coaches. This order must be strictly observed.

Ministry of Education Instructs Tongji University to Improve 206

(Nanjing, 5th) The Ministry of Education instructed National Tongji University, stating that the school had been inspected by the Ministry, and the submitted report had been reviewed. The school's teachers are experienced in teaching, committed to research, and very motivated. Students are diligent and disciplined, and the school spirit is quite strict, which is gratifying. However, the following points still need to be strictly improved: (1) The school's administrative organization does not have deans in each college, which is inconsistent with the university organization law. In the future, each college should set up a dean to manage college affairs, and the university should set up a Department of Academic Affairs with a director to handle all school teaching matters under the direction of the president. The original Department of Academic Affairs in each college should be abolished. The qualifications, treatment, and dismissal of hired professors should be properly formulated into regulations and submitted to the Ministry for approval. The library organization is too cumbersome, and the number of school workers exceeds the need, which can be reduced as appropriate. Training matters need to be added with specialists, actively guiding. The tables and statistics used by the school, after investigation, have a special German version, which is not appropriate. In the future, all should be changed to Chinese as the primary language. (2) The school's financial allocation method has more public funds than equipment costs, resulting in deviations from the Ministry's set standards. The affiliated high school's annual expenditure accounts for one-sixth of the school's total funding, which is quite high. However, the instruments, medicines, specimens, and necessary equipment for the surveying and civil engineering departments required for physics, chemistry, and biology experiments are still lacking. Reference books for each department are also insufficient. In the future, efforts should be made to economize on office expenses and reduce the funding for the affiliated high school to enrich equipment and benefit teaching. (3) The school's affiliated senior high school is divided into two colleges for management, which is inconvenient. The equipment for books and physics, chemistry, and biology is insufficient for application. The teaching method focuses on lectures and neglects experiments. The students' level, except for German, is quite uneven. The staff is not serious about handling affairs, and no one is responsible for guidance in training management. Dormitory order is especially disordered. The above aspects should be effectively rectified and improved. (4) The school's affiliated senior vocational school has achieved results. However, the physics and chemistry equipment and reference books are extremely simple. The mechanical and civil engineering experimental equipment is also imperfect. The Ministry increased the school's budget last year, which was designated to enrich the vocational school. This funding should be used to add equipment to facilitate teaching and experiments. In addition, the name of the affiliated school should be prefixed with the words "Industrial" to comply with the regulations. Except for the part about the medical school, which will be ordered to be complied with after a detailed review of the report, it is hereby ordered that the school strictly comply with and report.

After the Ministry of Education's Commissioners Arrived in Beiping, They Inspected Xiehe and Beida Medical Colleges in Detail, Investigating the Equipment Situation of Various Departments 207

(Special Dispatch from Beiping) The Ministry of Education is determined to rectify the various universities and colleges in North China, making reforms based on actual circumstances. Special inspection commissioners Xie Shuying, Zhu Zhanggeng, Sun Guofeng, and Li Xien have been dispatched to Beiping for inspection. Work began on the 25th, first inspecting medical schools, followed by other vocational schools and universities. The situations of various parties are recorded separately below.

Purpose of this Year's Inspection The purpose of this inspection by the Ministry of Education's commissioners is to review the progress of improving the instructions in the Ministry of Education's instructions to rectify various schools last year. Therefore, this inspection is not of an ordinary nature. In addition to a general inspection, this inspection will also discuss with the authorities of various schools the points to be noted in the future. All universities and colleges in the various provinces of North China must be inspected. Inspections will be held annually in the future, with South China and North China being held in two phases. The first phase will inspect higher education in South China, and the second semester will inspect higher education in North China.

Scheduled Inspection Itinerary The special inspection itinerary is scheduled for two months. They departed from Beijing on the 21st, arrived in Jinan on the 22nd, and inspected Qilu University and Medical School. They left Jinan on the 23rd, arrived in Beiping on the 24th, and began inspecting various schools in Beiping on the 25th. After staying in Beiping for three weeks to complete the inspection of various schools, they will go to Tianjin for inspection, and then return to Beiping, traveling south along the Pingjin Line. They will successively inspect Baoding, Kaifeng, Hankou, Anhui, and other places, and return to Beijing in May. Because the Shanghai area must be inspected in June, they must return to Beijing in May. This inspection is more complicated and the date is slightly shorter, so in terms of social interaction, apart from talking with the principals or deans of various schools, there is no time to take care of the rest.

Inspection of Xiehe Hospital Xie Shuying and others went to Xiehe Medical College for inspection at 9:00 AM on the 25th. After arriving at the college, they were received by Dean Gu Lin, Vice President Wang Gongshi, and others. After a short break, they were guided by Gu Lin to inspect the teaching affairs, starting from the Department of Anatomy and successively inspecting the departments of Biology, Physiology, Bacteriology, Pathology, Pharmacology, Ear, Nose, Throat, Obstetrics and Gynecology, Ophthalmology, Pediatrics, Internal Medicine, Surgery, Brain, Dentistry, X-Ray, Public Health, Dermatology, etc. They reviewed the equipment in detail. By 11:00 AM, the teaching affairs had been completely inspected. At 12:00 noon, Dean Gu Lin hosted a banquet to entertain them. At 2:00 PM, they continued to inspect the hospital's social service department, physical therapy institute, pharmacy, special wards, library, drawing room, and the statistics, bookkeeping, and income and expenditure of the General Affairs Office. The inspection was completed at 5:00 PM.

Inspection of Beida Medical College Ministry of Education inspection commissioners Xie Shuying, Sun Guofeng, Zhu Zhanggeng, and Li Xien went to the Medical College of Peking University outside Hepingmen Housun Park at 8:00 AM today (26th). Dean Wu Xiangfeng and Secretary Ma Zhidao received them. After learning the news, Peking University President Dui Songming also rushed to the scene by car to take care of everything. After a brief conversation, the inspection of teaching affairs began, starting from the Department of Biology and successively inspecting the departments of Physiology, Pharmacology, Bacteriology, Internal and External Medicine, Anatomy, Chemistry, Obstetrics and Gynecology, Pediatrics, etc. They asked in detail about equipment and teaching methods. Whenever they arrived at a department, the chief doctor was responsible for answering. By 10:00 AM, the inspection of the classrooms was completed. Then, they inspected the accounting, general affairs registration, and other administrative aspects. At 11:30 AM, accompanied by Xu and Wu, they went to the Public Health Office affiliated to the college in Xidan Hongmiao for inspection. At 12:00 noon, they went to the affiliated hospital of the college in Xidan Jieyin Hutong for lunch. During the meal, the commissioners asked in detail about the recent situation of the college and stated the points that the Ministry of Education had pointed out that should be noted in the future. After a short break after the meal, they continued to inspect the diagnosis and treatment of various departments of the affiliated hospital at 2:00 PM, including Internal and External Medicine, Pediatrics, Ear, Nose, Throat, Ophthalmology, Dermatology, Venereal Diseases, X-Ray, Physical Therapy, Nursing and Midwifery Training, and inspected the equipment, lighting, special wards, general wards, sanatorium wards, infectious disease wards, and the like. Because the inspection was more detailed, it did not end until 5:30 PM. They returned to the Central Hotel to rest.

Review of Zhongyuan College's Science Department The Ministry of Education's commissioners paid special attention to many points in this inspection of various schools. For example, if a certain problem had occurred or a request had been submitted to the Ministry of Education, it was included in this inspection. The private Zhongyuan College was originally China University, but was later changed to a college due to the lack of science department equipment. In recent years, through the efforts of President Wang Zhengting, a science department has been added, and the college has applied to the Ministry of Education for permission to restore the university. The Ministry of Education had previously sent commissioners Liu Shuqi, Ye Qisun, Chen Zhen, and others to inspect the college's science department equipment, but because the equipment was still insufficient, permission was not granted. Recently, after another reorganization, the college has again applied to restore the university. The Ministry of Education's commissioners will conduct a second inspection of the college's science department.

Shanghai City Literacy Education Committee Begins Operations; Literacy Methods Divided into Two Types; Jiangwan Designated as Experimental Zone 209

The Shanghai City Literacy Education Committee, since its establishment in the Municipal Government on the 1st of this month, has been actively working under the supervision of Director-General Tao Baichuan. The general office is currently located in the Municipal Zhengzhong Elementary School in the city center. Tao views this literacy education initiative as a pioneering undertaking requiring careful planning. His previous position as Chief of the Military Law Department of the Headquarters cannot be sustained concurrently, and he has already submitted his resignation to focus on this work. However, it is reported that Commander Wu has urged him to stay, granting him a short leave of absence temporarily. The current situation of the committee is explored below.

Key Planning Points The literacy education plan established by the committee targets the more than 500,000 illiterate citizens of this city. The methods have been revised and divided into two types: one is attending school for supplementary study, and the other is off-campus supplementary study. Regarding the first method, the committee plans to establish 300 literacy schools, each with one class, each class meeting six times, and each session lasting one hour. The municipal government will compel illiterate citizens to attend school for one hour daily for two months to graduate. If each school enrolls 50 people per session, one school can accommodate 200 people per month, and 300 schools can accommodate 60,000 people. If six sessions are held per year, the total enrollment can reach 540,000 people. The committee plans to conduct on-site surveys to compile a list of those unable to attend school for supplementary study. The second method, off-campus supplementary study, will be used. The committee will introduce Kuomintang party members, government officials, school teachers, or older students to provide individual guidance, and the committee will convene regular examinations. The committee has also designated Jiangwan as a pilot area and has appointed Jiang Wenbao, a specialist from the Municipal Education Bureau, as the director of the pilot area, it is said.

Major Schedule The general office of the committee has set April to June as the preparation period. A schedule of major events during the preparation period has been drafted, including: April 1st, the establishment of the committee, passing of important regulations, and the appointment of the Director-General and Deputy Director-General; April 4th, the Director-General and Deputy Director-General begin work, request the assignment of staff from the committee chairman, and establish the office; April 6th, the Jiangwan pilot area office is established; April 12th, surveys in the pilot area begin, along with widespread publicity; April 15th, literacy textbooks are sent for printing; April 21st, surveys in the pilot area conclude; April 22nd, preparations for the opening of literacy schools in the pilot area begin; April 28th, literacy textbooks are published; May 1st, literacy schools in the pilot area open, and offices in other districts are established; May 8th, surveys in other districts begin, along with expanded publicity; May 15th, enrollment for the literacy school teacher training institute begins; May 20th, entrance examinations for the training institute begin; May 21st, entrance examinations for the training institute conclude, and results are announced that evening; May 23rd, the training institute opens; May 31st, surveys in other districts conclude; June 23rd, the training institute concludes, and graduates are assigned to serve in various districts; June 24th, preparations for the opening of literacy schools in other districts begin; July 1st, the first session of literacy schools in other districts opens.

The institute will provide specialized sericulture technology training to meet the practical needs of sericulture improvement projects nationwide. The National Academic Work Advisory Office has been entrusted to handle the recruitment and examination process. In Shanghai, registration and examinations will be handled by the China Vocational Education Society at 80 Hualong Road. On the 11th, agricultural science majors will have specialized examinations in Biology, Fertilizer Science, Soil Science, Entomology, and Sericulture (choose three). On the 12th, mechanical engineering majors will have specialized examinations in Algebra, Geometry, Trigonometry (choose one), and Principles of Mechanics and Thermodynamics. Oral examinations will be held on the 19th and 20th. Results will be announced in the Shanghai Ta Kung Pao on the 26th. Groundbreaking Ceremony for Qingguang Elementary School Building

Preparations for the construction of the private Qingguang Elementary School on Fuli Road in the west of Shanghai are complete. Construction of the new school building began yesterday. The planned school building will be a three-story Western-style house with steel-reinforced concrete, a flat roof, red tiles, and red bricks. Each classroom will have three bays, providing ample light and spacious classrooms. A large auditorium, gymnasium, science hall, and small hospital are also planned. The design drawings for the entire school were created by the well-known architect Tao Guiyuan of this city. The construction contract was undertaken by Chen Yungui and Li Jinde of the Xieji Construction Company. Pu Junlin is responsible for managing the construction costs, income, and expenditures. Zhao Youliang, the school's organizer, visited various well-known Chinese and Western elementary schools in the city to observe the beautiful, durable, and developmentally appropriate desks and chairs for the school's interior, which will be selected, customized, and contracted out to the Qinde Woodworking Company. In addition to the new school building, there is also a 2.4-mu plot of land for use as a playground, garden, and lawn. Shen Weixiang has negotiated with various property owners to secure this land. It is also reported that enthusiastic educators in the city have provided special assistance to the school's fundraising efforts for the construction of the school building. Donations are being collected by the Shanghai City Bank's Ximen branch and will soon be concluded and reported to the Municipal Education Bureau for verification, it is said.

Liangjiang Basketball Team Passes Through Makassar; Defeats Zheng Yi Middle School 86-14 229

News of the Liangjiang Basketball Team's arrival in Java has spread, and various ports are making preparations to welcome them. Consul Wang De invited Zheng Yi Middle School to hold a friendly match when Liangjiang arrived. On the morning of March 12th, the team arrived in Makassar. The consul and his wife, representatives from various organizations and schools, and alumni of Liangjiang working in Makassar welcomed them on board. The meeting was very cordial. Consul Wang also provided several cars to transport the entire Liangjiang team to the consulate for rest and commemorative photos. The cars then drove around the city. At 12:00 noon, the consul hosted a banquet. At 2:00 PM, the principal of Zheng Yi welcomed them to visit the school and play a match. A crowd had gathered, eagerly awaiting the arrival of the Liangjiang team. Leaders of the Chinese community were also present, making it a very lively occasion. The match started at 2:00 PM, using men's rules. The seasoned Liangjiang team, renowned at home and abroad, put on a spectacular performance. Although the Zheng Yi team is known for its fierce and skilled players, facing Liangjiang proved too difficult. They were unable to mount any effective attacks. As a result, Liangjiang won 86-14, a huge difference that the Chinese community had not anticipated. Everyone cheered and applauded enthusiastically. After the match, a banquet was held. During the banquet, Principal Lu of Liangjiang gave a long speech, hoping that compatriots at home and abroad would unite and strive to advance sports in preparation for the revival of the nation. At 4:00 PM, the Liangjiang team had to board the ship to leave for Surabaya. The consul and his wife and female members of the community came to the dock to welcome them and presented them with flags and flower baskets as souvenirs. The alumni of the school, seeing the principal and classmates of their alma mater about to depart, were all very sad, with some even shedding tears, it is said.

The gold market yesterday was still mediocre, with limited transactions. After this, there was a slight pullback, but retail investor sentiment turned positive, and selling pressure was not significant, allowing buyers to operate. The price rose further at noon, but weakened slightly after the close. The after-market opened flat and weak, and trading was sluggish, with the market extremely stable. Although the Central Bank supplied gold, banks and Sassoon continued to maintain it, leading to a lack of momentum for decline and obstruction of rises, with a stable sentiment seeking supply and merely hovering. With large investors watching from the sidelines, there was a lack of support, causing selling pressure to permeate and the trend to suddenly dim. Grain: Flourishing Rice Arrivals in Shanghai South; Only Two or Three Numbers in Shanghai North 239

Yesterday, the source of each helper in Shanghai South suddenly surged, totaling nearly 50 numbers (nearly 10,000 stone in total), and the sales market was stagnant for both wholesale and retail. Only the Weihaiwei helper moved about 500 bags, so the overall situation became one of oversupply, and the market color showed a downward trend. As a result, each thick japonica rice fell by 2 jiao, and thin indica rice depreciated by 3 jiao. The decline was even more severe among those who closed, plummeting by 4 jiao, and Yinbian Yuan and Xie fell by 2 or 3 jiao respectively. There were two or three incoming boats from the various routes of He Xia in Shanghai North. Now that prices are plummeting, we must pay attention.

Investigation of Japanese Ban on Plant Imports 246

To prevent the introduction of plant diseases and insect pests from other countries and protect their own agriculture, many European and American countries have various prohibitions and inspection procedures. Some even use these measures to compensate for the inadequacy of tariff barriers and exclude agricultural imports from other countries. Japan also promulgated the Import and Export Plant Control Law on January 1, Showa 9 (1934), implementing inspection and control of imported plants. Looking around the world, there are few countries that have not implemented plant disease and insect pest inspections. However, our country, which is based on agriculture, has not yet implemented plant disease and insect pest inspections. The intangible losses suffered are incalculable. The types of plants prohibited and required to be inspected by Japan are listed below:

(1) Plants Prohibited from Import by Japan (Effective January 1, Showa 9 [1934], except for wheat straw, which is effective from February 1)

According to Article 7 of the Import and Export Plant Control Law, the Japanese government prohibits the import of plants and their packaging materials shipped from the regions listed in the table below. However, this does not apply to those used for testing and research, with the permission of the Minister of Agriculture and Forestry.
